When Are Medical Professionals Liable? The Hanafi Position on Cupper, Phlebotomist, and Kuhl-Applicer
Commentary on the rule that a cupper, phlebotomist, or kuhl-applicer is not liable unless they exceed the customary place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions required for a cupper, phlebotomist, or kuhl-applicer to avoid liability for harm, and apply them to new scenarios.

Core Idea
A medical professional is not liable for harm if two conditions are met: staying within customary practice and having permission.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a crucial area of Hanafi tort law: when do professionals performing inherently risky acts—like cupping, phlebotomy, and eye treatment—bear liability? The general principle is that an obligatory act does not coexist with guarantee. But the jurists identified two necessary conditions: non-exceeding the customary place and permission from the patient (or master). We will explore the proof, the exceptions, and the intra-Hanafi reconciliation of two narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central rule
The rule is that a cupper, phlebotomist, or kuhl-applicer does not guarantee (is not liable) if he does not exceed the customary place. Understand the basis: the act is obligatory by contract, and an obligatory act cannot coexist with guarantee.
This is analogous to a judge who administers punishment and the person dies—no liability.
2
Analyze the rationale
The act becomes obligatory because the professional undertook it by contract. However, the rule distinguishes between acts where harm can be controlled (like beating a garment) and those where it cannot (like phlebotomy, which depends on the patient's constitution). For the latter, liability is dropped unless exceeding custom.
The key exception: if the professional exceeds the customary place, he is liable for the excess.
3
Determine the exceptions
If the patient dies, the professional pays half diyya because death resulted from both a permitted act (the professional's work) and an unpermitted cause (the death itself). Also note the case of the circumciser cutting the prepuce: full/half diyya applies.
The death case is a proportional liability.
4
Reconcile two narrations
Al-Mukhtasar (Kanz al-Daqaiq) emphasizes non-exceeding; al-Jami' al-Saghir emphasizes permission. Al-Kafi reconciles: both conditions are required. If either is missing, liability is due.
This reconciliation is a hallmark of Hanafi usul: combining apparent contradictions.
5
Apply to new cases
Use the two-condition rule to decide liability in scenarios like tooth extraction (ordered tooth vs. connected tooth), kuhl application (wrong eye), and disputes between professional and patient.
The passage provides several furu' (sub-branches) for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رحمه الله : (ولا يضمن حجام أو فصاد أو بزاغ لم يتعد الموضع المعتاد) لأنه التزمه بالعقد فصار واجباً عليه والفعل الواجب لا يجامعه الضمان كما إذا حد القاضي أو عزر ومات المضروب بذلك إلا إذا كان يمكنه التحرز عن ذلك كدق الثوب فأمكن تقييده بالسليم بخلاف الفصد ونحوه فإنه ينبني على قوة الطبع وضعفه ولا يعرف ذلك بنفسه ولا ما يحتمله الجرح فلا يمكن تقييده بالسليم وهو غير الباري فسقط اعتباره إلا إذا جاوز المعتاد فيضمن الزائد. وهذا كله إذا لم يهلك، وإن هلك يضمن نصف دية النفس لأنه هلك بمأذون وغير مأذون فيضمن بحسابه حتى لو أن الختان قطع الحشفة وهو عضو كامل يجب عليه الدية نصف الدية وهي من أندر المسائل وأغربها حيث يجب الأكثر بالبرء وبالهلاك الأقل. وفي شرح الطحاوي: لو قطع الحشفة فعليه القصاص، ولو قطع بعض الحشفة فلا قصاص عليه، ولم يذكر ما يجب عليه . وفي الصغرى : تجب حكومة عدل. وفي الخلاصة : الكحال إذا صب الدواء في عين رجل فذهب ضوءه لم يضمن كالختان إلا إذا غلط، فإن قال رجلان إنه ليس بأهل وقال رجلان هو أهل لم يضمن، فإن كان في جانب الكمال واحد في جانب الآخر اثنان ،ضمن، ولو قال رجل للكحال دا وبشرط أن لا يذهب ، فذهب لم يضمن أمر رجلاً أن يقلع سنه فقلعه ثم اختلفا قال أمرتك أن تقلع غيره وقال الحجام أمرتني بقلع هذا القول قول الآمر ا هـ. وفي الظهيرية ولو بزغ واختلفا فالقول للآمر ويضمن القالع أرش .السن. وفي الخلاصة : ولو قلع ما أمره ولكن سن آخر متصل بهذا السن سقط ضمنه وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أن الضمان ينتفي بعدم المجاورة، وذكر في الجامع الصغير وحجامة العيد بأمر المولى حتى إذا لم يكن بأمر المولى يجب الضمان. قال في الكافي : عبارة المختصر ناطقة بعدم التجاوز وساكتة عن الإذن وعبارة الجامع الصغير ناطقة بالإذن ساكتة عن التجاوز فصار ما نطق به هذا بياناً لما سكت عنه الآخر، ويستفاد بمجموع الروايتين اشتراط عدم التجاوز والإذن لعدم وجوب الضمان حتى إذا عدم أحدهما أو كلامهما يجب الضمان ا هـ .
May Allah have mercy on him: (And a cupper, phlebotomist, or kuhl-applicer does not guarantee if he does not exceed the customary place) because he undertook it by contract, so it became obligatory upon him, and an obligatory act does not coexist with guarantee, as when the judge administers the prescribed punishment or discretion and the punished person dies from that, unless he could have avoided that, such as beating a garment where it is possible to restrict it to the sound part, unlike phlebotomy and the like, because it depends on the strength or weakness of the constitution and he himself does not know that or what the wound can bear, so it is not possible to restrict it to the sound part, and it is not the case that it is safe, so its consideration is dropped. Unless he exceeds the customary place, then he is liable for the excess. All this is if he does not die. And if he dies, he is liable for half the diyya of the person because he died by a permitted and an unpermitted act, so he is liable proportionally. Even if the circumciser cuts off the prepuce, which is a complete organ, he must pay the full diyya, half diyya. This is among the rarest and strangest issues, where more is due for healing and less for destruction. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: If he cuts off the prepuce, he is subject to qisas; if he cuts part of the prepuce, no qisas, and it is not mentioned what is due upon him. And in al-Sughra: a just compensation is due. And in al-Khulasa: If a kuhl-applicer puts medicine in a man's eye and his sight goes, he is not liable like the circumciser, unless he errs. If two men say he is not skilled and two men say he is skilled, he is not liable. If there is one on the side of perfection and two on the other side, he is liable. If a man says to the kuhl-applicer: Apply kuhl with the condition that it does not go, and it goes, he is not liable. A man orders another to extract his tooth, and he extracts it, then they dispute: one says 'I ordered you to extract another' and the other says 'You ordered me to extract this'; the saying is that of the orderer. In al-Zahiriyya: If he phlebotomized and they dispute, the saying is that of the orderer, and the extractor must pay the compensation for the tooth. In al-Khulasa: If he extracts what he was ordered, but another tooth connected to this tooth falls out, he is liable for it. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that liability is negated by non-exceeding. And it is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir that cupping of the male slave is by the master's permission; if it is not by the master's permission, liability is due. It is said in al-Kafi: The wording of al-Mukhtasar speaks of non-exceeding and is silent about permission; the wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir speaks of permission and is silent about non-exceeding. So what one speaks of clarifies what the other is silent about. From the combination of the two narrations, we deduce that both non-exceeding and permission are conditions for non-liability. If either one or both are absent, liability is due.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage covers the liability of specific professionals—cupper, phlebotomist, and kuhl-applicer—who perform acts that are likely to cause harm but are permissible by virtue of obligation. Since the act is obligatory (due to undertaking by contract), the general principle is that there is no liability for harm caused, because an obligatory act cannot coexist with guarantee. However, this principle has qualifications: if the professional exceeds the customary practice, he is liable for the excess. For example, if a cupper cuts beyond the usual place, he is liable for the additional harm. Furthermore, if the patient dies, the professional pays half the diyya because the death resulted from both a permitted act (the professional's work) and an unpermitted cause (the death itself). The passage then discusses specific cases from various sources: the circumciser cutting the prepuce (a full member) requires full diyya (half diyya? The text says 'full diyya, half diyya' indicating a complex calculation), then the kuhl-applicer, tooth extraction, and disputes. The conclusion from al-Kafi is that two conditions are necessary for non-liability: (1) not exceeding the customary practice, and (2) having permission. If either is missing, liability is due.

Key Terms
حجام (hajjam): A cupper who performs hijama (cupping therapy).
فصاد (fassad): A phlebotomist who performs venesection.
بزاغ (bazzagh): A kuhl-applicer who applies medicine to the eyes.
موضع معتاد (mawdi' mu'taad): The customary or standard location for a medical procedure.
دية (diyah): Blood money or compensation paid for homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A cupper performs a procedure within the usual area but without the patient's permission. According to the combined Hanafi position, what is the ruling?
A) He is not liable because he stayed within custom.
B) He is liable because permission is also required.
C) He is liable only if the patient dies.
D) He is not liable because the act was obligatory.

Key Takeaway
A cupper, phlebotomist, or kuhl-applicer is not liable for harm if they do not exceed the customary place and have permission; otherwise, liability applies.

The Specific Hired Worker's Right to Wage Upon Surrender
Commentary on the matn that the special hired worker deserves the wage by surrendering himself even if he does no work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the specific hired worker's entitlement to wage and explain the distinction from the common hired worker.

Core Idea
The specific hired worker's wage is for potential benefit, not actual work; surrender of self secures the wage.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the specific hired worker (ajir khas). The key principle is that he is hired to make his services available exclusively for a period. Therefore, his wage is earned by simply being available, regardless of whether work is actually performed. This contrasts with the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak), who is hired for a specific task and only gets paid upon delivery of completed work. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract type
Recognize that the passage deals with an ajir khas hired for a period, e.g., for a month for service or herding sheep.
2
State the ruling and its basis
The ajir khas deserves wage by surrendering himself (taslim nafsihi) during the period, whether he works or not, because the wage is in exchange for usufructs (manafi').
3
Note the condition
He deserves wage unless an impediment prevents him from enabling himself, such as illness or rain.
4
Distinguish from the ajir mushtarak
For the common hired worker, if work is undone by a third party before delivery, he loses his wage; but if the ajir khas undoes his own work, he must redo it.
5
Apply to scenarios
Consider examples: working for multiple employers, undoing work, and when the worker qualifies as specific (period mentioned first).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (والخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة وإن لم يعمل كمن استؤجر شهراً للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم) يعني الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة عمل أو لم يعمل . قال الأكمل وما يرد على تعريف الأجير المشترك يرد مثله على تعريف الخاص ا هـ . وسمى الأجير خاصاً ووحده لأنه يختص بالواحد وليس له أن يعمل لغيره ولأن منافعه صارت مستحقة للغير والأجر مقابل بها فيستحقه ما لم يمنع مانع من العمل كالمرض والمطر ونحو ذلك مما يمنع التمكين ولم يتعرض المؤلف إذا عمل المتعدد ونحن نبين ذلك . قال في المحيط : ولو أجر نفسه من غيره وعمل للأول والثاني استحق الأجر كاملاً على كل واحد منهما ولا يتصدق بشيء ويأثم ا هـ . قال صاحب الهداية : والأجر مقابل بالمنافع ولهذا يستحق الأجر عليه وإن نقض العمل . قال صاحب النهاية : نقض على البناء للمفعول بخلاف الأجير المشترك فإنه روي عن محمد في خياط خاط ثوب رجل فنقضه رجل قبل أن يقبضه رب الثوب فلا أجر للخياط لأنه لم يسلم العمل إلى رب الثوب، ولا يجبر الخياط أن يعيد العمل لأنه لو أجير لكان بحكم العقد الذي وقع في ذلك قد انتهى بتمام العمل، وإن كان الخياط هو الذي نقض فعليه أن يعيد العمل لأنه لما نقضه صار كأنه لم يحصل منه عمل، ومثله الإسكافي والملاح حتى إذا أراد الملاح رد السفينة منع من ذلك. وإنما يكون أجيراً خاصاً إذا شرط عليه أن لا يرعى لغيره أو ذكر المدة أولاً فإنه جعله خاصاً بأول كلامه حيث ذكر المدة أولاً . وقوله «لرعي غنمه» يحتمل أن يكون لايقاع العقد على العمل فيصير مشتركاً، ويحتمل أن يكون لبيان نوع العمل فإن الإجارة على المدة لا تصح ما لم يبين نوع العمل فلم
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the specific hired worker deserves the wage by surrendering himself during the period, even if he does not work, like one who is hired for a month for service or for herding sheep). That is, the specific hired worker deserves the wage by surrendering himself during the period, whether he works or not. Al-Akmal said: Whatever objection is raised against the definition of the common hired worker is similarly raised against the definition of the specific hired worker. He was called 'specific' because he is exclusive to one person and may not work for another, and because his usufructs become due to the other party and the wage is in exchange for them, so he deserves it as long as there is no impediment preventing work, such as illness, rain, etc., which prevent enabling. The author did not address if he worked for multiple persons; we will explain that. In al-Muhit: If he hired himself to someone else and worked for both the first and the second, he deserves the full wage from each and does not give charity from it, and he commits sin. The author of al-Hidaya said: The wage is in exchange for the usufructs, and therefore he deserves the wage even if he undoes the work. The author of al-Nihaya said: 'Undoing' (naqd) is passive; unlike the common hired worker, for it is narrated from Muhammad concerning a tailor who sewed a man's garment, and then someone else undid the stitching before the owner took delivery: the tailor has no wage because he did not deliver the work to the owner, and the tailor is not forced to redo the work because, if he were hired specifically, the contract would have been concluded by completion of work. And if the tailor himself undid it, he must redo it because when he undid it, it was as if no work occurred. Likewise the shoemaker and the boatman. Even if the boatman wants to return the boat, he is prevented from that. He is only a specific hired worker if he stipulated that he should not herd for others or if he mentioned the period first. This is because he made it specific by his initial words when he mentioned the period first. His statement 'for herding his sheep' could be for concluding the contract on the work, thus making him a common worker, or it could be for specifying the type of work, because a hiring on a period is not valid unless the type of work is specified. So...
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage discusses the specific (or special) hired worker (ajir khas), who is hired to make his services available exclusively for a period. The ruling is that he is entitled to the full wage simply by making himself available during the period, even if no work is actually performed. This is because the wage is in exchange for the usufruct (potential benefit) of the worker, not for actual output. The commentary then addresses definitions and exceptions: if the worker also works for another (violating the exclusivity), he deserves the full wage from each but commits a sin. The passage distinguishes between the specific hired worker and the common hired worker (ajir mushtarak). For the common hired worker, if the work is undone by a third party before delivery, the worker loses his wage because he did not deliver the work. But if the specific worker undoes his own work, he must redo it because the benefit was not delivered. Finally, the passage explains when a worker is considered specific: if the period is mentioned first in the contract, making him exclusive, even if the type of work is specified.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A specific hired worker who is hired exclusively for a period to make his services available, regardless of whether work is performed.
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A common hired worker who is hired for a specific task or piece of work, not for a period.
تسليم نفسه (taslim nafsihi): Surrendering himself, i.e., making himself available and capable of performing the work during the contracted period.
منافع (manafi'): Usufructs or benefits derived from the worker's service potential.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man hires a worker for one month to guard his sheep. The worker shows up every day but the sheep are not actually brought for the first week due to illness of the sheep. According to Hanafi, does the worker deserve wage for that week?
A) No, because he did not work.
B) Yes, because he surrendered himself.
C) Yes, only if he can prove he was available.
D) No, because the owner did not benefit.

Key Takeaway
A specific hired worker's wage is earned by his availability (surrender of self), not by actual work; this is because the wage compensates for the usufruct of his service potential.

Liability of the Oculist and Cupper
Clarifying liability conditions for medical professionals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions under which a hired medical professional avoids liability in Hanafi fiqh, and apply them to hypothetical scenarios.

Core Idea
A hired professional is liable if he acts without permission or exceeds the authorized scope.

We have seen that a hired worker (ajir) is generally not liable for damage arising from his work. But what about medical professionals like oculists and cuppers? This passage examines their liability and resolves an apparent tension between two key Hanafi texts. By analyzing the combined conditions of permission (idhn) and non-exceeding (tajawuz), we will derive the precise rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recall that an ajir (hired person) is not liable for loss or damage that occurs through his work, provided he acts within the scope of the hire. This is the baseline rule for the oculist and cupper.
Note: This rule applies to both specific and common ajirs in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Recognize the Exceptions
The passage lists exceptions: the professional becomes liable if he errs (ghalata) or exceeds the authorized scope (tajawaza). For example, an oculist who is not skilled (laysa bi-ahl) is liable if two witnesses attest to his incompetence.
Error includes incompetence or misapplication.
3
Extract the Two Key Conditions
From the combined narrations (al-Mukhtasar and al-Jami' al-Saghir), we deduce that avoidance of liability depends on two conditions: (1) the professional must have permission (idhn) from the patient or owner, and (2) he must not exceed the authorized area or action (tajawuz).
Permission alone is insufficient if he exceeds; non-exceeding alone is insufficient if he lacked permission.
4
Resolve the Apparent Contradiction
Al-Mukhtasar emphasizes non-exceeding but is silent on permission; al-Jami' al-Saghir emphasizes permission but is silent on exceeding. Al-Kafi explains that each text supplements the other, so both conditions are required.
This is a classic case of combining narrations (jam' bayn al-riwayatayn) in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply to Scenarios
Apply the combined rule: If a cupper pulls the correct tooth (permission + no exceeding) – no liability. If he pulls a different tooth (exceeding) – liable. If he acts without any order (no permission) – liable even if he causes no damage beyond the act itself.
The same applies to oculists and other similar professionals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الإجارة باب ضمان الأجير كمن استؤجر شهراً للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم ولا يضمن ما تلف في يده أو بعمله وصح بصره الخلاصة : الكحال إذا صب الدواء في عين رجل فذهب ضوءه لم يضمن كالختان إلا إذا غلط، فإن قال رجلان إنه ليس بأهل وقال رجلان هو أهل لم يضمن، فإن كان في جانب الكمال واحد في جانب الآخر اثنان ،ضمن، ولو قال رجل للكحال دا وبشرط أن لا يذهب ، فذهب لم يضمن أمر رجلاً أن يقلع سنه فقلعه ثم اختلفا قال أمرتك أن تقلع غيره وقال الحجام أمرتني بقلع هذا القول قول الآمر ا هـ. وفي الظهيرية ولو بزغ واختلفا فالقول للآمر ويضمن القالع أرش .السن. وفي الخلاصة : ولو قلع ما أمره ولكن سن آخر متصل بهذا السن سقط ضمنه وظاهر عبارة المؤلف أن الضمان ينتفي بعدم المجاورة، وذكر في الجامع الصغير وحجامة العيد بأمر المولى حتى إذا لم يكن بأمر المولى يجب الضمان. قال في الكافي : عبارة المختصر ناطقة بعدم التجاوز وساكتة عن الإذن وعبارة الجامع الصغير ناطقة بالإذن ساكتة عن التجاوز فصار ما نطق به هذا بياناً لما سكت عنه الآخر، ويستفاد بمجموع الروايتين اشتراط عدم التجاوز والإذن لعدم وجوب الضمان حتى إذا عدم أحدهما أو كلامهما يجب الضمان ا هـ .
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on Liability of the Ajir. Like one who is hired for a month for service or for grazing sheep, and he is not liable for what is lost in his hand or from his work, and his sight is sound. The summary: The oculist, if he pours medicine into a man's eye and his light goes, is not liable like the circumciser, unless he errs. If two men say he is not skilled and two men say he is skilled, he is not liable. If on one side there is one complete [skilled] and on the other side two, he is liable. If a man says to the oculist, 'This and on condition that it does not go,' and it goes, he is not liable. A man orders another to pull his tooth, so he pulls it, then they disagree: one says 'I ordered you to pull a different one' and the cupper says 'You ordered me to pull this one' – the statement is that of the orderer. In al-Zahiriyya: If he does cupping and they disagree, the statement is of the orderer, and the puller is liable for the tooth's compensation. In al-Khulasa: If he pulls what he was ordered but another tooth connected to this tooth falls, he is liable for it. The apparent wording of the author is that liability is negated by lack of exceeding [the area]. And it is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir: The cupping of the Eid [slaughter] is by the master's order, so if it is not by the master's order, liability is required. Al-Kafi said: The wording of al-Mukhtasar speaks of non-exceeding and is silent about permission, while the wording of al-Jami' al-Saghir speaks of permission and is silent about exceeding. So what one stated becomes an explanation of what the other left silent. From the combination of the two narrations, the condition for lack of liability is the absence of both exceeding and permission, such that if one of them or both are absent, liability is required.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory expansion on the general rule that an ajir (hired worker) is not liable for damage caused by his work unless he transgresses or acts without permission. The author uses the examples of the oculist (kahhal) and cupper (hajjam) to illustrate. The oculist is not liable for loss of sight if he applies medicine properly and is skilled. The cupper is not liable if he pulls the tooth he was ordered to pull. However, if he exceeds the area of the tooth (e.g., pulls an adjacent innocent tooth), he is liable. Similarly, if he acts without explicit permission (e.g., cupping a sacrificial animal without the owner's order), he is liable. The key principle derived from combining narrations is that two conditions must be met for the professional to avoid liability: (1) he must not exceed the authorized scope (al-tajawuz), and (2) he must have permission (al-idhn). If either condition is missing, he becomes liable for damages.

Key Terms
الكحال (al-kahhal): A medical professional who applies kohl or medicine to the eye.
الحجام (al-hajjam): A cupper who performs bloodletting or tooth extraction.
الإذن (al-idhn): Permission from the owner or patient.
التجاوز (al-tajawuz): Exceeding the authorized scope of the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the combined condition for an oculist or cupper to avoid liability?
A) Permission (idhn) alone is sufficient.
B) Non-exceeding (tajawuz) alone is sufficient.
C) Both permission and non-exceeding must be present.
D) The professional must be an expert (ahl) and have permission.

Key Takeaway
A hired medical professional avoids liability only when he acts with permission and does not exceed the authorized scope; if either condition is missing, he must compensate for damages.

Special Hire (Ajir Khas): Definition, Wages, and Liability
Defining the special hire and explaining his amanah and liability for loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a special hire (ajir khas) and a common hire (ajir mushtarak) and explain the liability of a special hire for losses according to the Hanafi school, including the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A special hire is a trustee (amin) – wages for availability, not work, and no liability for accidental loss.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the legal status of a special hire (ajir khas). Unlike a common hire who is paid for specific work output, the special hire is compensated simply for making himself available. This distinction has critical implications for liability: as a trustee, the special hire is not responsible for accidental losses, though there is a well-known disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples on the boundaries of 'accidental.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses a contract of hire (ijara) where the worker is hired for a fixed period. The ruling is that the special hire deserves his wage simply by making himself available for the period, regardless of whether work is performed.
The matn states: 'والخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة وإن لم يعمل'
2
Note the condition of being a special hire
The passage explains that a hire is special only if the contract wording gives precedence to the period (e.g., 'for a month') or explicitly restricts the worker to one employer. If work is mentioned first, it becomes a common hire.
This distinction is key for determining liability.
3
Understand the default rule of liability
The special hire is an amin (trustee). He is not liable for accidental loss of the subject matter (e.g., sheep dying naturally, drowning, being eaten by a predator) because such events are beyond his control.
Al-Muhit: 'فإذا كان خاصاً فماتت شاة أو أكلها سبع أو غرقت في نهر فلا ضمان على الراعي لأنه أمين'
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the special hire is not liable for losses such as a runaway sheep, theft while asleep, or involuntary mating, citing that these are beyond control (umur ghayr mumkin al-taharruz). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) deem these preventable and thus hold the hire liable.
The passage gives multiple scenarios: 'ندت واحدة', 'سرق غنم وهو نائم', 'نزى الفحل بدون فعله'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and any tarjih
The practical difference: under Imam, the hire pays nothing; under Sahibayn, he compensates. Later fatwa often prefer Sahibayn's view for stronger protection of the owner's property, but the text does not explicitly resolve the dispute.
The student should recognize both as valid positions within the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (والخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة وإن لم يعمل كمن استؤجر شهراً للخدمة أو لرعي الغنم) يعني الأجير الخاص يستحق الأجر بتسليم نفسه في المدة عمل أو لم يعمل . قال الأكمل وما يرد على تعريف الأجير المشترك يرد مثله على تعريف الخاص ا هـ . وسمى الأجير خاصاً ووحده لأنه يختص بالواحد وليس له أن يعمل لغيره ولأن منافعه صارت مستحقة للغير والأجر مقابل بها فيستحقه ما لم يمنع مانع من العمل كالمرض والمطر ونحو ذلك مما يمنع التمكين ولم يتعرض المؤلف إذا عمل المتعدد ونحن نبين ذلك . قال في المحيط : ولو أجر نفسه من غيره وعمل للأول والثاني استحق الأجر كاملاً على كل واحد منهما ولا يتصدق بشيء ويأثم ا هـ . قال صاحب الهداية : والأجر مقابل بالمنافع ولهذا يستحق الأجر عليه وإن نقض العمل . قال صاحب النهاية : نقض على البناء للمفعول بخلاف الأجير المشترك فإنه روي عن محمد في خياط خاط ثوب رجل فنقضه رجل قبل أن يقبضه رب الثوب فلا أجر للخياط لأنه لم يسلم العمل إلى رب الثوب، ولا يجبر الخياط أن يعيد العمل لأنه لو أجير لكان بحكم العقد الذي وقع في ذلك قد انتهى بتمام العمل، وإن كان الخياط هو الذي نقض فعليه أن يعيد العمل لأنه لما نقضه صار كأنه لم يحصل منه عمل، ومثله الإسكافي والملاح حتى إذا أراد الملاح رد السفينة منع من ذلك. وإنما يكون أجيراً خاصاً إذا شرط عليه أن لا يرعى لغيره أو ذكر المدة أولاً فإنه جعله خاصاً بأول كلامه حيث ذكر المدة أولاً . وقوله «لرعي غنمه» يحتمل أن يكون لايقاع العقد على العمل فيصير مشتركاً، ويحتمل أن يكون لبيان نوع العمل فإن الإجارة على المدة لا تصح ما لم يبين نوع العمل فلم يعتبر حكم الكلام الأول بالاحتمال ولو قدم ذكر العمل وأخر المدة بأن قال ارع غنمي شهراً كان أجيراً مشتركاً لأنه جعله مشتركاً بأول كلامه بإيقاع العقد على العمل. وقوله «شهراً» يحتمل أن يكون لايقاع العقد على المدة فيكون خاصاً، ويحتمل أن يكون لتقدير العمل في المدة فلا يتغير أول كلامه بالاحتمال ما لم يصرح بخلافه. وفي المحيط : فإذا كان خاصاً فماتت شاة أو أكلها سبع أو غرقت في نهر فلا ضمان على الراعي لأنه أمين ولا ينقص من الأجر بحسابها لأن المعقود عليه تسليم نفسه وقد وجد . ولهذا لو سلم نفسه ولم يأمره بالرع تجب الأجرة وهو يصدق فيما يدعيه من الهلاك مع اليمين، ولو سلم إلى الراعي عدداً فأراد أن يزيد عليه والراعي يطيقه فله ذلك استحساناً لأن المستحق عليه الرعي بقدر ما يطيق لا رعي أغنام بعينها حتى قلنا في الظئر : لو استأجرها لإرضاع صبي فأراد أن يرضع صب صبياً آخر ليس له لأن العقد وقع على العمل وفيه زيادة عمل. ولو كان الراعي أجيراً مشتركاً لكان حكمه حكم الظئر لتعلق العقد بالمسمى فلا يزيد عليه ويلزمه رعي الأولاد وما بيع منها سقط من الأجر بحسابه، ولو شرط عليه رعي الأولاد صح استحساناً لأن هذه الجهالة غير مفضية إلى المنازعة راع مشترك خلط الأغنام فالقول في التمييز للراعي مع يمينه إن جهل صاحبه، وإن جهل الراعي يضمن قيمة الكل لأن الخلط استهلاك شرط على المشترك أن يأتي بعلامة الميت إن لم يأت فهو ضامن وليس للراعي أن ينزي على الغنم إلا بإذن مالكها، فإن فعل فعطب ضمن لأن هذا ليس من الرعي فإن نزى الفحل بدون فعله لم يضمن عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن لأنه مما يمكن الاحتراز عنه ندت واحدة فخلف على الباقي إن تبعها فلا ضمان عليه عند الإمام لأنه ترك حفظها بعذر وعندهما يضمن ولو سرق غنم وهو نائم لم يضمن عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن ولو ذبح الراعي شاة خوفاً عليها ضمن قيمتها يوم الذبح . قال :مشايخنا : هذا إذا كان يرجى حياتها، وإن كان لا لا يرجى يضمن لأنه مأذون فيه في هذه الحالة. عطب بعض الغنم فقال المالك شرطت عليه أن ترعى في مكان كذا غير هذا المكان وقال الراعي شرطت هذا المكان فالقول قول المالك والبينة للراعي، وهذا عند الأمام. وعندهما يضمن ولا يأخذ المصدق من الراعي، فإن أخذ منه فلا ضمان لأنه ليس في وسعه دفع السلطان والهلاك إذا كان بأمر لا يمكن التحرز عنه لا يضمن بالإجماع جعل الأجر لبنها وصوفها فالإجارة فاسدة للجهالة في اللبن والصوف والراعي ضامن لما أصاب من لبنها وصوفها . ا هـ.
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'And the special [hire] deserves the wage by surrendering himself for the period even if he does not work, like one who is hired for a month for service or for grazing sheep.' Meaning the special hire deserves the wage by surrendering himself for the period, whether he works or not. Al-Akmal said: What is objected to the definition of the common hire, a similar objection is made to the definition of the special. He called it special and singular because it is restricted to one person and he may not work for another, and because his benefits become due to another, and the wage is in exchange for them, so he deserves it as long as there is no preventing excuse like sickness, rain, etc., which prevent enablement. The author did not address if he works for multiple; we will clarify that. Al-Muhit said: If he hires himself to another and works for the first and second, he deserves the full wage from each, and he does not give charity anything, but he sins. The author of al-Hidayah said: The wage is in exchange for benefits, therefore he deserves the wage even if the work is undone. The author of al-Nihayah said: 'Undone' is passive, unlike the common hire, for it is narrated from Muhammad about a tailor who sewed a man's garment then a man undid it before the owner took possession; the tailor has no wage because he did not deliver the work to the owner, and the tailor is not compelled to redo the work because the contract ended with completion of work. But if the tailor himself undid it, he must redo it because by undoing it, it becomes as if no work occurred. Similarly for the cobbler and the boatman; if the boatman wants to return the boat, he is prevented. One is a special hire only if it is stipulated that he not graze for another, or if the period is mentioned first, because he makes it special by his initial statement by mentioning the period first. His saying 'for grazing his sheep' could be for effecting the contract on the work, making it common, or for specifying the type of work, for a hire for a period is not valid unless the type of work is specified, so the initial statement's ruling is not considered due to probability. If he puts the work first and delays the period, saying 'Graze my sheep for a month,' he is a common hire because he made it common by his initial statement by effecting the contract on the work. His saying 'a month' could be for effecting the contract on the period, making it special, or for measuring the work in the period, so his initial statement is not changed by probability unless he explicitly states otherwise. In al-Muhit: If he is special and a sheep dies, or a wolf eats it, or it drowns in a river, there is no liability on the shepherd because he is an amin, and his wage is not reduced proportionally because the contracted subject is his surrendering of himself, which has occurred. For this, if he surrenders himself and does not command the grazing, the wage is due, and he is believed regarding the claim of loss with an oath. If he delivers a number [of sheep] to the shepherd and then wants to increase, and the shepherd can bear it, he may do so by istihsan because what is due from him is grazing to the extent he can bear, not grazing specific sheep. We say regarding the wet nurse: if he hires her to suckle a boy and then wants her to suckle another boy, she may not, because the contract is on the work and it involves additional work. If the shepherd is a common hire, his ruling is like the wet nurse because the contract is tied to the specified object; he may not increase, and he must graze the offspring, and for what is sold, his wage is reduced proportionally. If the condition of grazing the offspring is stipulated, it is valid by istihsan because this uncertainty does not lead to dispute. A common shepherd who mixes the flocks: the statement regarding distinguishing is that of the shepherd with his oath if the owner is unknown. If the shepherd is ignorant, he guarantees the value of all because mixing is destruction. A condition is set on the common [hire] to bring a sign of the dead; if he does not, he is liable. The shepherd may not mate the sheep except with the owner's permission; if he does and it causes harm, he is liable because this is not part of grazing. If the stallion mates without his action, he is not liable according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], but according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] he is liable because it can be guarded against. If one [sheep] runs away and follows the rest, there is no liability on him according to Imam because he left guarding with an excuse; according to the two, he is liable. If sheep are stolen while he is asleep, he is not liable according to Imam; according to the two, he is liable. If the shepherd slaughters a sheep fearing for it, he guarantees its value on the day of slaughter. Our mashayikh said: This is if its life was hoped for; if not, he is not liable because he is permitted in that case. Some sheep are destroyed and the owner says 'I stipulated that you graze in such a place, not this place' and the shepherd says 'I stipulated this place'; the statement is that of the owner, and the evidence is on the shepherd. This is according to Imam. According to the two, he is liable, and the tax collector does not take from the shepherd; if he takes, there is no liability because he cannot resist the authority. Loss that cannot be guarded against is not liable by consensus. Making the wage [from] its milk and wool: the hire is void due to uncertainty in the milk and wool, and the shepherd is liable for what is taken from its milk and wool.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an expanded explanation of the special hire (ajir khas). The author quotes the matn that the special hire deserves his full wage simply by making himself available for the entire period, regardless of whether he actually performs work. This is because the contract is on his readiness (taslim al-nafs), not on the actual work output. The commentator then clarifies that the special hire is an amin (trustee) and does not guarantee loss unless there is negligence or transgression (tajawuz). The passage then distinguishes between a special hire and a common hire (ajir mushtarak) based on the wording of the contract: if the period is mentioned first, he is special; if the work is mentioned first, he is common. Numerous examples follow: the shepherd whose sheep die from natural causes is not liable; if he mixes flocks, he may be liable; differences between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) are detailed on issues like mating, runaway sheep, and theft while sleeping. The general rule is that the special hire is not liable for losses beyond his control, but the common hire has stricter liability because he is a guarantor (damin) of the work product.

Key Terms
الأجير الخاص (al-ajir al-khas): A hired worker who is available for a specific period for one employer, entitled to wages for availability, not just work done
أمين (amin): A trustee; not liable for loss without negligence or transgression
الأجير المشترك (al-ajir al-mushtarak): A hire who contracts for a specific work outcome and may work for multiple clients

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a special hire (ajir khas) contract for grazing sheep, if a sheep dies naturally, what is the shepherd's liability according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) He must compensate the owner because he is a guarantor (damin).
B) He is not liable because he is an amin (trustee).
C) He is liable only if he was negligent.
D) He must pay half the value.

Key Takeaway
A special hire is an amin (trustee) entitled to wages for availability and is not liable for accidental loss, though the Sahibayn differ on certain preventable losses.

Ajir Khas vs Ajir Mushtarak: Contract Wording Determines Liability
Ruling on classifying hired workers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a hire contract as ajir khas or ajir mushtarak based on the wording and state the consequence for liability.

Core Idea
The order of mentioning work vs time decides if the worker is a trustee or a guarantor.

In Hanafi fiqh, the liability of a hired worker depends critically on whether he is classified as a special employee (ajir khas) or a contract worker (ajir mushtarak). This distinction is determined by the wording of the contract, as the passage explains. By mastering this foundational rule, you will understand why some shepherds are liable for loss and others are not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract wording
Look at the phrase used: does the employer mention the work first (e.g., 'Graze my sheep for a month') or the time first (e.g., 'Be my shepherd for a month')?
The passage specifically considers the phrase 'Graze my sheep for a month' as work-first.
2
Apply the classification rule
If work is mentioned first, the worker is ajir mushtarak (contract worker), regardless of the following time phrase. If time is mentioned first, he is ajir khas (special employee).
Probability in the later phrase does not change the classification unless explicitly contradicted.
3
Understand the liability consequence
Ajir mushtarak is a yad al-daman (hand of guarantee) and is liable for loss. Ajir khas is an amin (trustee) and not liable for accidental loss.
This difference is the practical outcome of the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدرهم يعتبر حكم الكلام الأول بالاحتمال ولو قدم ذكر العمل وأخر المدة بأن قال ارع غنمي شهراً كان أجيراً مشتركاً لأنه جعله مشتركاً بأول كلامه بإيقاع العقد على العمل. وقوله «شهراً» يحتمل أن يكون لايقاع العقد على المدة فيكون خاصاً، ويحتمل أن يكون لتقدير العمل في المدة فلا يتغير أول كلامه بالاحتمال ما لم يصرح بخلافه. وفي المحيط : فإذا كان خاصاً فماتت شاة أو أكلها سبع أو غرقت في نهر فلا ضمان على الراعي لأنه أمين ولا ينقص من الأجر بحسابها لأن المعقود عليه تسليم نفسه وقد وجد . ولهذا لو سلم نفسه ولم يأمره بالرع تجب الأجرة وهو يصدق فيما يدعيه من الهلاك مع اليمين، ولو سلم إلى الراعي عدداً فأراد أن يزيد عليه والراعي يطيقه فله ذلك استحساناً لأن المستحق عليه الرعي بقدر ما يطيق لا رعي أغنام بعينها حتى قلنا في الظئر : لو استأجرها لإرضاع صبي فأراد أن يرضع صب صبياً آخر ليس له لأن العقد وقع على العمل وفيه زيادة عمل. ولو كان الراعي أجيراً مشتركاً لكان حكمه حكم الظئر لتعلق العقد بالمسمى فلا يزيد عليه ويلزمه رعي الأولاد وما بيع منها سقط من الأجر بحسابه، ولو شرط عليه رعي الأولاد صح استحساناً لأن هذه الجهالة غير مفضية إلى المنازعة راع مشترك خلط الأغنام فالقول في التمييز للراعي مع يمينه إن جهل صاحبه، وإن جهل الراعي يضمن قيمة الكل لأن الخلط استهلاك شرط على المشترك أن يأتي بعلامة الميت إن لم يأت فهو ضامن وليس للراعي أن ينزي على الغنم إلا بإذن مالكها، فإن فعل فعطب ضمن لأن هذا ليس من الرعي فإن نزى الفحل بدون فعله لم يضمن عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن لأنه مما يمكن الاحتراز عنه ندت واحدة فخلف على الباقي إن تبعها فلا ضمان عليه عند الإمام لأنه ترك حفظها بعذر وعندهما يضمن ولو سرق غنم وهو نائم لم يضمن عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن ولو ذبح الراعي شاة خوفاً عليها ضمن قيمتها يوم الذبح . قال :مشايخنا : هذا إذا كان يرجى حياتها، وإن كان لا لا يرجى يضمن لأنه مأذون فيه في هذه الحالة. عطب بعض الغنم فقال المالك شرطت عليه أن ترعى في مكان كذا غير هذا المكان وقال الراعي شرطت هذا المكان فالقول قول المالك والبينة للراعي، وهذا عند الأمام. وعندهما يضمن ولا يأخذ المصدق من الراعي، فإن أخذ منه فلا ضمان لأنه ليس في وسعه دفع السلطان والهلاك إذا كان بأمر لا يمكن التحرز عنه لا يضمن بالإجماع جعل الأجر لبنها وصوفها فالإجارة فاسدة للجهالة في اللبن والصوف والراعي ضامن لما أصاب من لبنها وصوفها . ا هـ مختصراً.
By a dirham: the ruling of the first statement is considered with probability. If he mentioned the work first and postponed the time by saying 'Graze my sheep for a month,' he is a contract worker because he made it joint (mushtarak) by his first statement, placing the contract on the work. His word 'month' may be for placing the contract on the time, making it specific (khas), or for measuring the work in the time. His first statement is not changed by probability unless he explicitly contradicts it. In al-Muhit: If it is specific and a sheep dies or a wolf eats it or it drowns in a river, there is no liability on the shepherd because he is a trustee; no abatement of the wage correspondingly because the contracted object is the surrender of his self, which occurred. Hence if he surrendered himself and he did not order him to graze, the wage is due, and he is believed in his claim of destruction with oath. If he surrendered a number to the shepherd and then wanted to increase it and the shepherd can handle it, he may do so by istihsan because what is due upon him is grazing to the extent he can, not grazing specific sheep. Thus we said regarding the wet nurse: If he hired her to nurse a boy and then wanted her to nurse another boy, she may not, because the contract fell on the work and there is extra work. If the shepherd was a contract worker, his ruling would be like the wet nurse because the contract is tied to the named, so he cannot increase; he must graze the offspring, and from what is sold, the wage is reduced proportionally. If he stipulated grazing the offspring, it is valid by istihsan because this uncertainty does not lead to dispute. A contract shepherd mixed the sheep: the statement is the shepherd's with oath if he is ignorant of the owner; if the shepherd is ignorant, he guarantees the value of all because mixing is destruction. The contract worker is required to bring a mark of the dead; if he does not, he is liable. The shepherd may not mount the ram on the sheep except with the owner's permission; if he does and it causes damage, he is liable because this is not grazing. If the ram mounts without his action, he is not liable according to Imam; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is liable because it is avoidable. One strayed and left the rest; if it followed, no liability on him according to Imam because he left guarding due to an excuse; according to the two, he is liable. If sheep were stolen while he slept, no liability according to Imam; according to the two, he is liable. If the shepherd slaughtered a sheep fearing for it, he guarantees its value on the day of slaughter. Our mashayikh said: This is if its life was hoped for; if not, he does not guarantee because he is permitted in this case. Some sheep perished, and the owner said 'I stipulated that you graze in such a place, not this place,' and the shepherd said 'I stipulated this place,' the statement is the owner's and the evidence is the shepherd's. This is according to Imam. According to the two, he is liable. And the collector (musaddiq) does not take from the shepherd; if he took, no liability because he cannot repel the sultan. If destruction occurs due to an unpreventable matter, no liability by consensus. If the wage was made her milk and wool, the ijarah is invalid due to uncertainty in the milk and wool, and the shepherd is liable for what he took of her milk and wool. End, abridged.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (al-Muhit) presents a series of rulings concerning the contract shepherd (ajir mushtarak), who is hired to perform a specific task (grazing) rather than to serve a specific time. The key principle is that a contract worker guarantees (yadman) the property in his possession because he is a 'yad al-daman' (hand of guarantee), unlike the special employee (ajir khas) who is a trustee (amin). The passage begins by explaining how to determine if the worker is contract or special based on how the contract is phrased: if the work is mentioned first, he is contract; if time is mentioned first, he is special. Then it lists numerous scenarios: death of animals by natural causes leads to no liability for the special employee (he is amin), but for the contract worker, the rulings differ—for example, if he mixes flocks and cannot distinguish, he guarantees the value of all. The passage also records intra-Hanafi disagreements: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the ram mounts without the shepherd's action, or if a stray sheep leads others astray, or if sheep are stolen while he sleeps, there is no liability; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold liability in these cases because the shepherd could have prevented them. The final section deals with invalid wage terms (milk and wool) leading to invalid ijarah, and the shepherd is liable for what he consumed.

Key Terms
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A worker hired to perform a specific task (e.g., grazing) for multiple clients; he is a yad al-daman and liable for loss.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): An employee hired exclusively for a period; he is an amin (trustee) and does not guarantee loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an employer says 'Transport my goods for a month,' what is the classification?
A) Ajir mushtarak, because 'transport' (work) is mentioned first.
B) Ajir khas, because 'for a month' (time) is mentioned after the work.
C) Ajir khas, because the word 'month' indicates a specific period.
D) Ajir mushtarak, because the work is mentioned first, and the time is only for measurement.

Key Takeaway
The classification of a hired worker as ajir khas or ajir mushtarak hinges on whether the contract mentions work first or time first, affecting liability for loss.

Liability of the Special Employee (Ajir Khas) as a Trustee
Ruling on ajir khas liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the ajir khas is an amin and not liable for accidental loss, and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
The ajir khas is a trustee—no liability for accidental loss, wage still due.

Once we know the worker is ajir khas (special employee), the passage details his liability status: he is an amin (trustee) like a depositee. This means he is not liable for losses such as death, wolf eat, or drowning, and he is believed on oath. The reason is that his wage is for surrendering his time, not for delivering a result.

Guided Path
1
Confirm the worker is ajir khas
The passage begins with 'If it is specific (khas)', meaning the contract is for a period, not a task.
This follows from the previous distinction.
2
Identify the loss scenarios
The text lists: a sheep dies, a wolf eats it, or it drowns. These are accidental, unpreventable losses.
The worker is not at fault.
3
Apply the ruling: no liability
Because the worker is an amin, he does not guarantee accidental loss. The wage is still due because he surrendered his time.
The contract is on the self, not on the result.
4
Note the evidentiary rule
The worker is believed on oath if he claims the loss occurred, because he is a trustee.
This is consistent with the principle that trustees are believed.

Commentary

Key Terms
أمين (amin): A trustee who holds property with permission; not liable unless negligent.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): An employee hired exclusively for a period; he is an amin (trustee) and does not guarantee loss.

Why is the ajir khas not liable for the death of a sheep?
A) Because the contract is void.

Key Takeaway

Mixing of Flocks and Liability of the Contract Shepherd
Ruling on liability for mixing flocks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that mixing flocks is destruction, making the contract shepherd liable if he cannot distinguish the owners.

Core Idea
Mixing flocks is destruction—contract shepherd guarantees all if he is ignorant of owners.

When a contract shepherd (ajir mushtarak) mixes the sheep of different owners, his liability depends on his knowledge. The passage provides a clear rule: if the shepherd knows the owners, he is believed with oath; if he is ignorant, he guarantees the value of all because mixing is considered a form of destruction (istihlak).

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation: mixing flocks
The shepherd, who is ajir mushtarak, mixes sheep belonging to different owners.
Mixing here means he cannot tell which sheep belong to which owner.
2
Check the shepherd's knowledge
The text distinguishes two cases: (a) the shepherd is ignorant of which sheep belong to whom (jahil al-sahib), and (b) the shepherd knows the owners but cannot distinguish physically.
Actually the text says 'إن جهل صاحبه' meaning the shepherd is ignorant of the owner of particular sheep, vs 'إن جهل الراعي' meaning the shepherd is ignorant (of the distinction).
3
Apply the ruling
If the shepherd is ignorant of the owners, he is believed with his oath that he does not know, and he is not liable. If the shepherd is ignorant of the distinction (i.e., he knows the owners but cannot tell which sheep is which), he guarantees the value of all because mixing is equivalent to destroying them.
The text: 'فالقول في التمييز للراعي مع يمينه إن جهل صاحبه، وإن جهل الراعي يضمن قيمة الكل لأن الخلط استهلاك'
4
Understand the rationale
Mixing that prevents returning specific sheep to their owners is like destroying them (istihlak). Therefore, the contract shepherd, who is a yad al-daman, must pay the value of all the sheep.
This is consistent with his position as guarantor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لأنه أمين ولا ينقص من الأجر بحسابها لأن المعقود عليه تسليم نفسه وقد وجد . ولهذا لو سلم نفسه ولم يأمره بالرع تجب الأجرة وهو يصدق فيما يدعيه من الهلاك مع اليمين، ولو سلم إلى الراعي عدداً فأراد أن يزيد عليه والراعي يطيقه فله ذلك استحساناً لأن المستحق عليه الرعي بقدر ما يطيق لا رعي أغنام بعينها حتى قلنا في الظئر : لو استأجرها لإرضاع صبي فأراد أن يرضع صب صبياً آخر ليس له لأن العقد وقع على العمل وفيه زيادة عمل. ولو كان الراعي أجيراً مشتركاً لكان حكمه حكم الظئر لتعلق العقد بالمسمى فلا يزيد عليه ويلزمه رعي الأولاد وما بيع منها سقط من الأجر بحسابه، ولو شرط عليه رعي الأولاد صح استحساناً لأن هذه الجهالة غير مفضية إلى المنازعة راع مشترك خلط الأغنام فالقول في التمييز للراعي مع يمينه إن جهل صاحبه، وإن جهل الراعي يضمن قيمة الكل لأن الخلط استهلاك شرط على المشترك أن يأتي بعلامة الميت إن لم يأت فهو ضامن وليس للراعي أن ينزي على الغنم إلا بإذن مالكها، فإن فعل فعطب ضمن لأن هذا ليس من الرعي فإن نزى الفحل بدون فعله لم يضمن عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن لأنه مما يمكن الاحتراز عنه ندت واحدة فخلف على الباقي إن تبعها فلا ضمان عليه عند الإمام لأنه ترك حفظها بعذر وعندهما يضمن ولو سرق غنم وهو نائم لم يضمن عند الإمام، وعندهما يضمن ولو ذبح الراعي شاة خوفاً عليها ضمن قيمتها يوم الذبح . قال :مشايخنا : هذا إذا كان يرجى حياتها، وإن كان لا لا يرجى يضمن لأنه مأذون فيه في هذه الحالة. عطب بعض الغنم فقال المالك شرطت عليه أن ترعى في مكان كذا غير هذا المكان وقال الراعي شرطت هذا المكان فالقول قول المالك والبينة للراعي، وهذا عند الأمام. وعندهما يضمن ولا يأخذ المصدق من الراعي، فإن أخذ منه فلا ضمان لأنه ليس في وسعه دفع السلطان والهلاك إذا كان بأمر لا يمكن التحرز عنه لا يضمن بالإجماع جعل الأجر لبنها وصوفها فالإجارة فاسدة للجهالة في اللبن والصوف والراعي ضامن لما أصاب من لبنها وصوفها . ا هـ مختصراً.
By a dirham: the ruling of the first statement is considered with probability. If he mentioned the work first and postponed the time by saying 'Graze my sheep for a month,' he is a contract worker because he made it joint (mushtarak) by his first statement, placing the contract on the work. His word 'month' may be for placing the contract on the time, making it specific (khas), or for measuring the work in the time. His first statement is not changed by probability unless he explicitly contradicts it. In al-Muhit: If it is specific and a sheep dies or a wolf eats it or it drowns in a river, there is no liability on the shepherd because he is a trustee; no abatement of the wage correspondingly because the contracted object is the surrender of his self, which occurred. Hence if he surrendered himself and he did not order him to graze, the wage is due, and he is believed in his claim of destruction with oath. If he surrendered a number to the shepherd and then wanted to increase it and the shepherd can handle it, he may do so by istihsan because what is due upon him is grazing to the extent he can, not grazing specific sheep. Thus we said regarding the wet nurse: If he hired her to nurse a boy and then wanted her to nurse another boy, she may not, because the contract fell on the work and there is extra work. If the shepherd was a contract worker, his ruling would be like the wet nurse because the contract is tied to the named, so he cannot increase; he must graze the offspring, and from what is sold, the wage is reduced proportionally. If he stipulated grazing the offspring, it is valid by istihsan because this uncertainty does not lead to dispute. A contract shepherd mixed the sheep: the statement is the shepherd's with oath if he is ignorant of the owner; if the shepherd is ignorant, he guarantees the value of all because mixing is destruction. The contract worker is required to bring a mark of the dead; if he does not, he is liable. The shepherd may not mount the ram on the sheep except with the owner's permission; if he does and it causes damage, he is liable because this is not grazing. If the ram mounts without his action, he is not liable according to Imam; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is liable because it is avoidable. One strayed and left the rest; if it followed, no liability on him according to Imam because he left guarding due to an excuse; according to the two, he is liable. If sheep were stolen while he slept, no liability according to Imam; according to the two, he is liable. If the shepherd slaughtered a sheep fearing for it, he guarantees its value on the day of slaughter. Our mashayikh said: This is if its life was hoped for; if not, he does not guarantee because he is permitted in this case. Some sheep perished, and the owner said 'I stipulated that you graze in such a place, not this place,' and the shepherd said 'I stipulated this place,' the statement is the owner's and the evidence is the shepherd's. This is according to Imam. According to the two, he is liable. And the collector (musaddiq) does not take from the shepherd; if he took, no liability because he cannot repel the sultan. If destruction occurs due to an unpreventable matter, no liability by consensus. If the wage was made her milk and wool, the ijarah is invalid due to uncertainty in the milk and wool, and the shepherd is liable for what he took of her milk and wool. End, abridged.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (al-Muhit) presents a series of rulings concerning the contract shepherd (ajir mushtarak), who is hired to perform a specific task (grazing) rather than to serve a specific time. The key principle is that a contract worker guarantees (yadman) the property in his possession because he is a 'yad al-daman' (hand of guarantee), unlike the special employee (ajir khas) who is a trustee (amin). The passage begins by explaining how to determine if the worker is contract or special based on how the contract is phrased: if the work is mentioned first, he is contract; if time is mentioned first, he is special. Then it lists numerous scenarios: death of animals by natural causes leads to no liability for the special employee (he is amin), but for the contract worker, the rulings differ—for example, if he mixes flocks and cannot distinguish, he guarantees the value of all. The passage also records intra-Hanafi disagreements: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the ram mounts without the shepherd's action, or if a stray sheep leads others astray, or if sheep are stolen while he sleeps, there is no liability; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold liability in these cases because the shepherd could have prevented them. The final section deals with invalid wage terms (milk and wool) leading to invalid ijarah, and the shepherd is liable for what he consumed.

Key Terms
استهلاك (istihlak): Destruction or consumption, rendering property irrecoverable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of mixing, when does the contract shepherd guarantee the value of all sheep?
A) When he is ignorant of the owners.
B) When he is ignorant of the distinction (cannot separate).
C) When he deliberately mixed.
D) Only if a sheep dies.

Key Takeaway
A contract shepherd who mixes flocks and cannot separate them is liable for the value of all sheep, as mixing is considered destruction.

Unauthorized Actions and Intra-Hanafi Disputes on Shepherd's Liability
Rulings on unauthorized acts and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a shepherd is liable for unauthorized acts and contrast the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa with the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).

Core Idea
Shepherd liable for unauthorized acts unless unpreventable; Imam Abu Hanifa excuses unpreventable losses, Sahibayn do not.

The passage details several scenarios where a contract shepherd does something without permission or faces an unavoidable event. In each case, Imam Abu Hanifa often finds no liability if the event was unpreventable, while the Two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the shepherd liable because he could have prevented it. Understanding this intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is crucial for applying the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
List the unauthorized acts
The passage mentions: mounting the ram without permission (causing damage), straying sheep that leads others away, sheep stolen while sleeping, and slaughtering a sheep fearing for its life.
These are acts outside the mandate of grazing.
2
State the general rule
If the shepherd does an unauthorized act that causes harm, he is liable. However, if the harm occurs without his direct action (e.g., ram mounts on its own), there is disagreement.
The rule is that the shepherd is a yad al-daman, but he is not liable for unpreventable acts.
3
Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam holds that if the ram mounts without the shepherd's action, if a stray sheep follows another, or if sheep are stolen while he sleeps, he is not liable because these are unpreventable.
The key concept is that he has an excuse (udhr).
4
Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold the shepherd liable in these cases because he could have taken precautions (e.g., neutering the ram, better fencing, more vigilance).
They view these as avoidable.
5
Slaughtering out of fear
If the shepherd slaughters a sheep fearing for its life, he is liable unless there was no hope of recovery. The later scholars (mashayikh) said if life was not hoped for, no liability.
This is a concession.

Source Text

Commentary

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A legally recognized excuse that removes liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, is the contract shepherd liable if sheep are stolen while he is asleep?
A) Yes, because he should stay awake.
B) No, because sleep is an excuse.
C) Yes, because he is a yad al-daman.
D) No, because the owner should have secured the sheep.

Key Takeaway
The contract shepherd is liable for unauthorized acts, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on unpreventable losses: Imam Abu Hanifa excuses, the Two hold liable.

Invalid Wage Terms and Disputes in Ijarah
Ruling on invalid wages and dispute resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when an ijarah contract becomes invalid due to uncertainty in the wage and determine the consequence (liability for benefit taken).

Core Idea
Uncertainty in wage (milk, wool) invalidates the contract; the shepherd is liable for what he took.

If the wage for the shepherd is set as the milk and wool of the sheep, the contract becomes invalid (fasid) because of uncertainty (jahala) in these items. The passage then states that the shepherd is liable for any milk or wool he consumed. Additionally, the passage covers a dispute over the grazing location: the owner's word is taken, and the shepherd must provide evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the invalid wage term
The wage is specified as 'her milk and wool'—these are unknown in quantity and quality at the time of contract.
This is more than minor uncertainty; it renders the ijarah fasid.
2
Apply the ruling for fasid ijarah
The contract is invalid. However, if the shepherd has taken some milk or wool, he must pay the equivalent value (daman) because he consumed the owner's property without valid right.
The shepherd is liable for what he actually took.
3
Handle the location dispute
If the owner and the shepherd disagree on the agreed grazing location, the owner's statement is taken (qawl qawl al-malik), and the shepherd must provide evidence to prove his claim.
This follows the principle that the owner is more credible in matters of their property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

In al-Muhit: If it is specific and a sheep dies or a wolf eats it or it drowns in a river, there is no liability on the shepherd because he is a trustee; no abatement of the wage correspondingly because the contracted object is the surrender of his self, which occurred. Hence if he surrendered himself and he did not order him to graze, the wage is due, and he is believed in his claim of destruction with oath. If he surrendered a number to the shepherd and then wanted to increase it and the shepherd can handle it, he may do so by istihsan because what is due upon him is grazing to the extent he can, not grazing specific sheep. Thus we said regarding the wet nurse: If he hired her to nurse a boy and then wanted her to nurse another boy, she may not, because the contract fell on the work and there is extra work. If the shepherd was a contract worker, his ruling would be like the wet nurse because the contract is tied to the named, so he cannot increase; he must graze the offspring, and from what is sold, the wage is reduced proportionally. If he stipulated grazing the offspring, it is valid by istihsan because this uncertainty does not lead to dispute. A contract shepherd mixed the sheep: the statement is the shepherd's with oath if he is ignorant of the owner; if the shepherd is ignorant, he guarantees the value of all because mixing is destruction. The contract worker is required to bring a mark of the dead; if he does not, he is liable. The shepherd may not mount the ram on the sheep except with the owner's permission; if he does and it causes damage, he is liable because this is not grazing. If the ram mounts without his action, he is not liable according to Imam; according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he is liable because it is avoidable. One strayed and left the rest; if it followed, no liability on him according to Imam because he left guarding due to an excuse; according to the two, he is liable. If sheep were stolen while he slept, no liability according to Imam; according to the two, he is liable. If the shepherd slaughtered a sheep fearing for it, he guarantees its value on the day of slaughter. Our mashayikh said: This is if its life was hoped for; if not, he does not guarantee because he is permitted in this case. Some sheep perished, and the owner said 'I stipulated that you graze in such a place, not this place,' and the shepherd said 'I stipulated this place,' the statement is the owner's and the evidence is the shepherd's. This is according to Imam. According to the two, he is liable. And the collector (musaddiq) does not take from the shepherd; if he took, no liability because he cannot repel the sultan. If destruction occurs due to an unpreventable matter, no liability by consensus. If the wage was made her milk and wool, the ijarah is invalid due to uncertainty in the milk and wool, and the shepherd is liable for what he took of her milk and wool. End, abridged.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from the commentary (al-Muhit) presents a series of rulings concerning the contract shepherd (ajir mushtarak), who is hired to perform a specific task (grazing) rather than to serve a specific time. The key principle is that a contract worker guarantees (yadman) the property in his possession because he is a 'yad al-daman' (hand of guarantee), unlike the special employee (ajir khas) who is a trustee (amin). The passage begins by explaining how to determine if the worker is contract or special based on how the contract is phrased: if the work is mentioned first, he is contract; if time is mentioned first, he is special. Then it lists numerous scenarios: death of animals by natural causes leads to no liability for the special employee (he is amin), but for the contract worker, the rulings differ—for example, if he mixes flocks and cannot distinguish, he guarantees the value of all. The passage also records intra-Hanafi disagreements: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if the ram mounts without the shepherd's action, or if a stray sheep leads others astray, or if sheep are stolen while he sleeps, there is no liability; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold liability in these cases because the shepherd could have prevented them. The final section deals with invalid wage terms (milk and wool) leading to invalid ijarah, and the shepherd is liable for what he consumed.

Key Terms
الجهالة (al-jahala): Uncertainty or ambiguity that may invalidate a contract if it leads to dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the wage is set as the sheep's milk and wool?
A) The contract is valid and the shepherd owns the milk and wool.
B) The contract is invalid (fasid) and the shepherd is liable for what he took.
C) The contract is void (batil) and no work is owed.
D) The contract is valid but the shepherd must give the milk and wool to the owner.

Key Takeaway
Uncertainty in the wage (e.g., milk, wool) invalidates the ijarah contract and makes the shepherd liable for any benefit taken.

Non-Liability of the Special Employee (Ajir Khas)
Explanation of non-liability for special employee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two bases for the non-liability of the special employee and apply the ruling to scenarios of accidental loss and intentional transgression.

Core Idea
The special employee is an amin — he does not guarantee loss unless he intentionally transgresses.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the special employee (ajir khas) is not liable for damage to the hired item or for loss caused by his work. The ruling is supported by consensus (ijma) and analogy with a trustee. Understanding this distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for distinguishing between trust-based and guarantee-based possession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and scenarios
State the ruling: the special employee does not guarantee loss. Identify the two scenarios: loss in hand (the item perishes while in his custody) and loss by his work (damage occurs during the performance of work).
The passage addresses both 'ما تلف في يده' and 'ما تلف بعمله'.
2
Analyze the proof for loss in hand
The proof is consensus (ijma): the item is an amana (trust) because it was taken with the owner's permission, so the holder is not liable. The commentator notes this is clear according to Imam Abu Hanifa and also accepted by the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), though they rely on istihsan for the contract worker.
The passage mentions 'فلا يضمن بالإجماع'.
3
Analyze the proof for loss by work
The usufruct is owned by the hirer; the worker is his deputy. The wage is not in exchange for the work itself but for making the usufruct available, so damage during work is not guaranteed. This is supported by the fact that the worker deserves wages even if he does not work.
The passage uses 'فلأن المنافع صارت مملوكة للمستأجر'.
4
Identify the exception for transgression
If the employee intentionally causes corruption (ta'addi), he is liable, just like a depositee. This is the only case where guarantee applies.
The passage says 'إلا إذا تعمد الفساد فيضمن بالتعدي'.
5
Understand the sharh expansion
The commentator expands the matn by providing the underlying reasoning and linking to the distinction between special and common employee. He also refers to al-Muhit for further application in crafts.
This is an expansion probe (textual_operation_tag) with additional details from the Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يضمن ما تلف في يده أو بعمله) أما الأول فلأن العين أمانة في يده لأنه قبضها بإذن مالكها فلا يضمن بالإجماع وهذا ظاهر على قول الإمام، وكذا عندهما لأن تضمين الأجير المشترك كان نوع استحسان وقد تقدم وجهه والأجير الخاص يعمل في بيت المستأجر ولا يقبل الأعمال من غيره أخذا فيه بالقياس وأما الثاني فلأن المنافع صارت مملوكة للمستأجر وأمره بالصرف إلى ملكه فصح وصار نائباً عنه وصار فعله منقولاً إليه لأنه فعله بنفسه، ولأن البدل ليس بمقابلة العمل بدليل أنه يستحق الأجر وإن لم يعمل، وهذا لأن المبيع وهي سليمة وإنما الخرق في العمل الذي هو تسليم المنفعة وذلك غير معقود عليه فلم يكن يضمن شيئاً ما هو عليه فلا يشترط فيه السلامة فلا يضمن ما تلف إلا إذا تعمد الفساد فيضمن بالتعدي كالمودع . وفي المحيط وعلى هذا التفصيل أما في الضمان تلميذ القصار وأجيره سائر الصنائع .
He (the author) said: (And he does not guarantee what is lost in his hand or by his work). As for the first (loss in his hand), because the item is a trust in his hand since he took it with the owner's permission, so he does not guarantee by consensus. This is clear according to Imam, and likewise according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because making the contract worker responsible was a type of istihsan, and its reasoning has preceded. The special employee works in the hirer's house and does not accept work from others, taking this by analogy. As for the second (loss by his work), because the usufructs become owned by the hirer and he ordered their use in his ownership, so it is valid and he becomes his deputy, and his action is attributed to him because he acts himself. And because the consideration is not in exchange for the work, evidenced by the fact that he deserves the wage even if he does not work. This is because the sold item (the usufruct) is sound, and the damage is in the work which is delivery of the usufruct, and that is not contracted upon, so he does not guarantee anything that occurs unless he intentionally causes corruption, then he guarantees due to transgression like the depositee. In al-Muhit: Upon this detail, concerning the guarantee of the fuller's apprentice and the employees of other crafts.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the matn: 'ولا يضمن ما تلف في يده أو بعمله' (he does not guarantee what is lost in his hand or by his work). The commentator explains two bases: First, for loss in his hand, the item is an amana (trust) because he took it with permission, so there is consensus (ijma') that a trustee is not liable. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa, and also of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, though they hold the contract worker liable by istihsan. The special employee (ajir khas) works exclusively for the hirer and does not accept other jobs, analogically like a depositee. Second, for loss by his work, the usufruct belongs to the hirer, and the worker is his deputy; the wage is for making the usufruct available, not for the specific physical action, so if damage occurs during work, it is not guaranteed unless he intentionally transgresses. The passage ends with a reference to al-Muhit applying this to various crafts.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajir khas): An employee hired for a specific time period, working exclusively for the hirer.
أمانة (amana): A trust; property held with permission, for which the holder is not liable unless negligent.
الإجماع (al-ijma): Consensus of scholars as a source of law.
تعدي (ta'addi): Transgression or misuse of the property leading to liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof for the non-liability of the special employee for loss in hand?
A) Istihsan
B) Qiyas
C) Ijma
D) Hadith

Key Takeaway
The special employee is an amin and does not guarantee accidental loss; liability only arises with intentional transgression.
