Contingent Wage in Ijarah: Type vs. Time (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Ruling on contingent wage for work type and time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a contingent wage arrangement in ijarah is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A wage contingent on the type of work is valid; on time it is invalid — but the Sahibayn disagree.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the limits of making the wage in an ijarah contract dependent on different outcomes. The author presents Imam Abu Hanifa's detailed position: valid for work type (e.g., Persian vs. Roman sewing) but invalid for time (today vs. tomorrow). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit both, while Zufar invalidates both. The key revolves around interpreting 'today' and 'tomorrow' literally or figuratively, and the comparison with sale's khiyar al-ta'yin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of contingency
Locate in the passage where the author distinguishes between contingency based on work type (e.g., Persian/Roman sewing) and contingency based on time (today/tomorrow). Note that the text says 'in the first' (type) is valid, but not in the second (time).
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling for each type
From the passage, extract that Imam holds: if the contingency is on work type (e.g., 'if you sew Persian, 1 dirham; if Roman, 2 dirhams'), it is valid. If on time (e.g., 'if today, 2 dirhams; if tomorrow, 1/2 dirham'), it is invalid.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn's position
The passage states that 'the two' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider both conditions permissible. Identify their reasoning: they interpret 'today' as specification (tawqit) and 'tomorrow' as suspense (ta'liq), so no two counter-values combine in one day.
4
Analyse the reasoning: figurative vs. literal interpretation
Follow the passage's detailed argument: According to Imam, 'today' must be interpreted figuratively as expediting (ta'jil) because a literal reading would conflict with specifying the work. 'Tomorrow' is taken literally as deferring (idafa). This creates a contradiction when both are mentioned together, leading to invalidity.
This step requires careful reading of the Arabic terms and their implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وصح ترديد الأجير بترديد العمل في الثوب نوعاً وزماناً في الأول) يعني يجوز أن يجعل الأجر متردداً بين تسميتين ويجعل العمل متردداً في الثوب بين نوعي العمل بأن يقول إن خطت فارسياً فبدرهم أو رومياً فبدرهمين أو صبغته بعصفر فبدرهم وبزعفران فبدرهمين. أو يجعل العمل متردداً بين زمانين بأن يقول إن خطته اليوم فبدرهمين وإن خطته غداً فبنصف درهم يجوز في الأول دون الثاني وهو معنى قوله «وزماناً في الأول». ويجوز التردد بين ثلاثة أشياء ولا يجوز بين أكثر كما تقدم. ولو قال المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى وصح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل نوعاً وزماناً في الأول فيما دون الأربعة» لكان أولى لأنه يفهم من الإطلاق أنه يصح في أكثر من الأربعة وهذا خيار التعين إلا أنه لا بد في البيع من اشتراط الخيار. وفي الإجارة لا يشترط ذلك، والفرق أن تحقيق الجهالة في البيع لا يرتفع إلا بإثبات الخيار بخلاف الإجارة واستشكل صاحب التسهيل هذا الفرق حيث قال أقول : الجهالة التي في طرف الأجرة ترتفع كما ذكر، أما التي في طرف العين المستأجرة فهي ثابتة وتفضي إلى المنازعة فينبغي أن لا يصح بدون شرط اليقين .ا.هـ. وهذا التفصيل في الزمان قول الإمام . وقالا : الشرطان جائزان. وقال زفر الشرطان فاسدان لأن الخياطة شيء واحد وقد ذكر لمقابلته بدلان فيكون مجهولاً ولهما أن ذكر اليوم للتوقيت وغداً للتعليق فلا يجتمع في كل يوم تسميتان وللإمام في الأول قال فارسياً ورومياً فسمى نوعين معلومين من العمل وسمى لكل منهما بدلاً معلوماً فيجوز للإمام أيضاً إذا كان الترديد في الزمان إن ذكر اليوم للتعجيل والغد للإضافة والكلام لحقيقته حتى يقوم دليل المجاز وقد قام الدليل على إرادة المجاز في ذكر اليوم وهو التعجيل لأن مرادهما الصحة وهو متعين في المجاز لأن تعين العمل مع التوقيت مفسد، فإن تعين العمل يوجب كونه أجيراً مشتركاً وتعين الوقت يوجب كونه خاصاً وبينهما تفاوت فلا تجتمعان فتعين المجاز كي لا يفسد فحملاه على التعجيل، وفي الغد لم يقم الدليل على إرادة المجاز بل قام الدليل على إرادة الحقيقة وهو الإضافة يعني في التعليق فتركاه على حقيقته، فإذا كان ذكر اليوم للتعجيل وذكر للإضافة لم يجتمع في اليوم إلا نسبة واحد فلم يفسد، فإذا خاطه اليوم فله الدراهم، واجتمع في غد تسميتان فوجب حمله على الإضافة، وهذا يناقض ما قدمه من أنه إن كان العمل أولاً فالزمان لغو أو الزمان أولاً فالعمل لغو فهو في الأول أجير مشترك
He (the author) said: (And it is valid to make the wage contingent by making the work contingent in the cloth, in type and time, in the first). Meaning: It is permissible to make the wage fluctuate between two names, and to make the work fluctuate in the cloth between two types of work, such as saying 'If you sew it Persian-style, then one dirham, or Roman-style, then two dirhams', or 'If you dye it with safflower, then one dirham, and with saffron, then two dirhams.' Or to make the work fluctuate between two times, such as saying 'If you sew it today, then two dirhams, and if you sew it tomorrow, then half a dirham.' It is valid in the first (type) but not in the second (time), and that is the meaning of his statement 'and time in the first.' It is permissible to fluctuate between three things, and not more than three, as earlier. If the author had said 'and it is valid to make the wage contingent by making the work contingent in type and time in the first, up to less than four,' it would have been better because from the absolute expression it is understood that it is valid in more than four, and this is khiyar al-ta'yin, but in sale it is necessary to stipulate the option. In ijarah, that is not required. The difference is that the elimination of uncertainty in sale is not achieved except by establishing the option, unlike ijarah. The author of al-Tashil found this difference problematic, saying: 'I say: the uncertainty on the side of the wage is removed as mentioned, but on the side of the hired item, it is fixed and leads to dispute, so it should not be valid without stipulating certainty.' End. This detail regarding time is the statement of Imam. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Both conditions are permissible. Zufar said: Both conditions are invalid because sewing is one thing and two counter-values are mentioned for it, making it uncertain. The two argue that mentioning today is for specification (tawqit) and tomorrow for suspense (ta'liq), so not two names are combined in one day. According to Imam in the first (type): he said Persian and Roman, thus naming two known types of work and naming for each a known counter-value, so it is valid. Also for Imam, when the fluctuation is in time, if he mentions today for expediting and tomorrow for deferring, and speech is for its literal meaning until evidence of figurative meaning appears. Evidence for the figurative meaning in mentioning today exists, which is expediting, because their intent is validity, and it is necessarily figurative because specifying the work with time is invalidating. Indeed, specifying the work makes him a contract worker, and specifying the time makes him specific, and the two are disparate and cannot combine, so the figurative meaning is adopted to avoid invalidity, so they interpret it as expediting. For tomorrow, no evidence for figurative meaning appears; rather evidence for literal meaning exists, which is deferring (i.e., suspense), so they keep it literal. Thus, if he speaks of today for expediting and of tomorrow for deferring, then on today only one ratio is present, so it does not become invalid. If he sews today, he gets the dirhams. On tomorrow, two names combine, so it must be interpreted as deferring. This contradicts what was earlier stated: if the work is given precedence, time is superfluous; if time is given precedence, work is superfluous; so in the first case he is a contract worker.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of making the wage (ajr) contingent on the type of work or the time of performance in an ijarah contract. The matn states: 'وصح ترديد الأجير بترديد العمل في الثوب نوعاً وزماناً في الأول' meaning it is valid to make the wage fluctuate by fluctuating the work, but only in the first of two categories (type) not the second (time). The commentary explains examples: if the client says 'if you sew Persian-style, one dirham; if Roman-style, two dirhams' it is valid. But if he says 'if you sew today, two dirhams; if tomorrow, half a dirham' it is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because it creates uncertainty in the counter-value. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider both conditions permissible, while Imam Zufar considers them both invalid. The detailed reasoning turns on whether the mention of 'today' and 'tomorrow' is literal (ta'wiq and ta'liq) or figurative (expediting). The passage also discusses the maximum number of options (three) and compares with sale (khiyar al-ta'yin). It ends with a contradiction noted in the previous commentary, which is left unresolved.

Key Terms
ترديد الأجر (tardid al-ajr): Making the wage contingent on different possible outcomes.
خيار التعين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option to choose which item to purchase in a sale, requiring explicit stipulation.
الجهالة (al-jahala): Uncertainty or ambiguity in contract terms.
التعجيل (al-ta'jil): Expediting the performance of the work.
الإضافة (al-idafa): Attribution or deferring; here used for the literal meaning of 'tomorrow' as suspense.
التوقيت (al-tawqit): Specification of time.
التعليق (al-ta'liq): Suspense or conditionality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, which of the following contingent wage arrangements is valid in ijarah?
A) If you sew today, two dirhams; if tomorrow, one dirham.
B) If you sew Persian-style, one dirham; if Roman-style, two dirhams.
C) If you return today, one dirham; if tomorrow, half dirham.
D) Both A and B are valid.

Key Takeaway
In ijarah, a wage contingent on the type of work is valid, but one contingent on time is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, due to the inability to reconcile the literal and figurative interpretations.

Variable Wage and Work in Ijarah: Type vs. Time
Intra-Hanafi dispute on variable wage and work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on variable wage and work in ijarah and apply Imam Abu Hanifa's figurative interpretation to determine validity in time-based variation.

Core Idea
Variable wage by type is valid; variable wage by time requires figurative interpretation to avoid uncertainty.

In ijarah (hire) contracts, parties sometimes agree on a wage that varies depending on the type of work or the time of performance. The Hanafi school debates whether such variation introduces fatal uncertainty (jahalah). This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute, focusing on when variable terms are permissible and how Imam Abu Hanifa's interpretation resolves potential conflicts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two forms of variation
The text distinguishes between varying the wage by varying the work in type (e.g., Persian vs. Roman stitching) and varying the wage by varying the time of performance (e.g., today vs. tomorrow). Recognize that type variation is unanimously valid among the Hanafis.
Type variation involves distinct works; time variation involves the same work at different times.
2
State the three Hanafi positions on time variation
Imam Abu Hanifa allows it only if 'today' is interpreted as expediting and 'tomorrow' as suspension. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allow both conditions unconditionally. Zufar rejects both conditions as invalid.
Note the spectrum of views: from strict (Zufar) to lenient (Sahibayn), with Imam's middle path.
3
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning for time variation
Imam argues that literal reading of both 'today' and 'tomorrow' would combine two wages for one work, causing uncertainty. However, the parties' intention to make a valid contract is evidence (dalil) that 'today' is meant figuratively as expediting, removing uncertainty. 'Tomorrow' retains its literal meaning of suspension because the lower wage indicates a delay penalty, so only one wage applies each day.
This use of figurative interpretation (majaz) to avoid contract corruption is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.
4
Distinguish the type case from the time case
In the type case, two works are separate contracts, so no uncertainty arises. In the time case, the work is one, so literal interpretation would create two wages for the same work. Hence the need for figurative interpretation.
This distinction (tafriq) is crucial to understanding the different rulings.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Imam's view, if the worker stitches on the second day, he gets the like wage (ujr al-mithl) not exceeding the lower named wage. Under Sahibayn, he gets the named wage for that day. Under Zufar, the contract is void. These practical outcomes determine the mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi is Imam Abu Hanifa's view, as it avoids total invalidity while mitigating uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وصح ترديد الأجير بترديد العمل في الثوب نوعاً وزماناً في الأول ) يعني يجوز أن يجعل الأجر متردداً بين تسميتين ويجعل العمل متردداً في الثوب بين نوعي العمل بأن يقول إن خطت فارسياً فبدرهم أو رومياً فبدرهمين أو صبغته بعصفر فبدرهم وبزعفران فبدرهمين. أو يجعل العمل متردداً بين زمانين بأن يقول إن خطته اليوم فبدرهمين وإن خطته غداً فبنصف درهم يجوز في الأول دون الثاني وهو معنى قوله «وزماناً في الأول». ويجوز التردد بين ثلاثة أشياء ولا يجوز بين أكثر كما تقدم. ولو قال المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى وصح ترديد الأجر بترديد العمل نوعاً وزماناً في الأول فيما دون الأربعة» لكان أولى لأنه يفهم من الإطلاق أنه يصح في أكثر من الأربعة وهذا خيار التعين إلا أنه لا بد في البيع من اشتراط الخيار. وفي الإجارة لا يشترط ذلك، والفرق أن تحقيق الجهالة في البيع لا يرتفع إلا بإثبات الخيار بخلاف الإجارة واستشكل صاحب التسهيل هذا الفرق حيث قال أقول : الجهالة التي في طرف الأجرة ترتفع كما ذكر، أما التي في طرف العين المستأجرة فهي ثابتة وتفضي إلى المنازعة فينبغي أن لا يصح بدون شرط اليقين .ا.هـ. وهذا التفصيل في الزمان قول الإمام . وقالا : الشرطان جائزان. وقال زفر الشرطان فاسدان لأن الخياطة شيء واحد وقد ذكر لمقابلته بدلان فيكون مجهولاً ولهما أن ذكر اليوم للتوقيت وغداً للتعليق فلا يجتمع في كل يوم تسميتان وللإمام في الأول قال فارسياً ورومياً فسمى نوعين معلومين من العمل وسمى لكل منهما بدلاً معلوماً فيجوز للإمام أيضاً إذا كان الترديد في الزمان إن ذكر اليوم للتعجيل والغد للإضافة والكلام لحقيقته حتى يقوم دليل المجاز وقد قام الدليل على إرادة المجاز في ذكر اليوم وهو التعجيل لأن مرادهما الصحة وهو متعين في المجاز لأن تعين العمل مع التوقيت مفسد، فإن تعين العمل يوجب كونه أجيراً مشتركاً وتعين الوقت يوجب كونه خاصاً وبينهما تفاوت فلا تجتمعان فتعين المجاز كي لا يفسد فحملاه على التعجيل، وفي الغد لم يقم الدليل على إرادة المجاز بل قام الدليل على إرادة الحقيقة وهو الإضافة يعني في التعليق فتركاه على حقيقته، فإذا كان ذكر اليوم للتعجيل وذكر للإضافة لم يجتمع في اليوم إلا نسبة واحد فلم يفسد، فإذا خاطه اليوم فله الدراهم، واجتمع في غد تسميتان فوجب حمله على الإضافة، وهذا يناقض ما قدمه من أنه إن كان العمل أولاً فالزمان لغو أو الزمان أولاً فالعمل لغو فهو في الأول أجير مشترك وفي الثاني أجير خاص، فإذا خاطه في غد فله أجر مثله لا يزاد على نصف درهم بخلاف الفارسية والرومية لأنهما عقدان مختلفان لم يجتمعا فافترقا ويشكل على ما علل به في اليوم والغد مسألة الراعي فإنها جمع فيها بين ذكر الوقت والعمل وتصح الإجارة بالاتفاق، ولا يحمل الوقت على غير معناه الحقيقي في قول أحد بل يعتبر أجيراً مشتركاً إن وقع ذكر العمل أولاً وأجيراً وحده إن وقع ذكر الوقت أو لا كما ذكر في الذخيرة والمحيط . فعدلنا فلك عن قال صاحب الكافي : وفي المسألة إشكال على قول الإمام حيث جعل ذكر اليوم للتعجيل ههنا حتى أجاز العقد، وفي مسألة الخياط جعله للتوقيت وأفسد العقد. والجواب أن ذكر اليوم حقيقة للتوقيت فيحمل عليه حتى يقوم الدليل على المجاز وهو نقصان الأجر بسبب التأخير الحقيقة ولم نعمم هناك وكان التوقيت مراداً ففسد العقد.
He (the author) said: (And it is valid to make the hired worker variable by making the work variable in the cloth, in type and time, in the first). That is, it is permissible to make the wage variable between two named amounts, and to make the work variable in the cloth between two types of work, such as saying: if you stitch it Persian-style then for a dirham, or Roman-style then for two dirhams; or dye it with safflower then for a dirham, and with saffron then for two dirhams. Or to make the work variable between two times, such as saying: if you stitch it today then for two dirhams, and if you stitch it tomorrow then for half a dirham; it is valid in the first but not in the second, and this is the meaning of his saying 'and time in the first'. And it is permissible to vary between three things, but not more, as previously stated. If the author had said 'and it is valid to make the wage variable by making the work variable in type and time, in the first, within less than four', it would have been better, because from the absolute expression it is understood that it is valid for more than four. And this is an option of specification (khiyar al-ta'yin), but in sale it requires stipulating the option, while in hire it is not required. The difference is that the removal of uncertainty (jahalah) in sale is only achieved by establishing the option, unlike hire. The author of al-Tashil found this difference problematic, saying: 'I say: the uncertainty on the side of the wage is removed as mentioned, but as for the uncertainty on the side of the hired object (al-'ayn al-musta'jarah), it is established and leads to dispute, so it should not be valid without a condition of certainty.' End quote. And this distinction regarding time is the view of Imam (Abu Hanifa). They (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: both conditions are permissible. Zufar said: both conditions are invalid because stitching is one thing and two compensations are mentioned for it, so it is unknown. Their (the Sahibayn's) argument is that mentioning 'today' is for timing (tawqit) and 'tomorrow' is for suspension (ta'liq), so two named amounts do not combine in a single day. And for Imam, in the first case (type) he said 'Persian' and 'Roman', thus naming two known types of work and naming for each a known compensation, so it is valid. Also for Imam, regarding the time case, if mentioning 'today' is for expediting (ta'jil) and 'tomorrow' for addition (idafa), and speech is for its literal meaning until evidence for figurative meaning appears, and evidence has appeared for figurative meaning in mentioning 'today', which is expediting, because their intention is validity, and it is determined as figurative because specifying the work along with timing would corrupt, for specifying the work makes him a common worker (ajir mushtarak) and specifying the time makes him a private worker (ajir khas), and they differ, so they cannot combine, so figurative interpretation is necessitated to avoid corruption, so they interpreted it as expediting. For 'tomorrow', no evidence for figurative meaning appeared, rather evidence for literal meaning appeared, which is addition (i.e., suspension), so they left it on its literal meaning. Thus, if mentioning 'today' is for expediting and 'tomorrow' for addition, only one wage applies today, so it does not corrupt. If he stitches today, he gets the dirhams. On tomorrow, two wages combine, so it must be interpreted as addition. This contradicts his earlier statement that if the work is primary, time is redundant; or if time is primary, work is redundant. Thus, in the first (time case?) he is a common worker, and in the second a private worker. If he stitches tomorrow, he gets the like wage (ujr al-mithl) not exceeding half a dirham, unlike the Persian and Roman cases because they are two different contracts that did not combine, so they differ. And the case of the shepherd (al-ra'i) poses a difficulty for this reasoning in the today/tomorrow case, for it combines mentioning time and work, and the hire is unanimously valid, and time is not interpreted non-literally in any view, rather he is considered a common worker if mention of work comes first, and a private worker if mention of time comes first, as mentioned in al-Dhakhirah and al-Muhit. So we modified? [unclear]. Al-Kafi said: There is a problem with Imam's position: here he made mentioning 'today' for expediting to validate the contract, but in the tailor case (mas'alat al-khayyat) he made it for timing and invalidated the contract. The answer: mentioning 'today' is literally for timing, so it is applied accordingly until evidence for figurative meaning appears, which is the decrease in wage due to delay as a literal fact; we did not generalize there, and timing was intended, so the contract was invalid.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of making the wage and the work variable (taraddad) in an ijarah contract. The author explains the ruling from the matn: it is valid to vary the wage by varying the work in type (e.g., Persian vs. Roman stitching) and in time (e.g., today vs. tomorrow), but only in the first meaning (type) while time is disputed. The text clarifies that variation by type is valid because each type is a distinct work with a distinct wage, removing uncertainty. Variation by time is more problematic because the same work is associated with two different wages depending on when it is performed, leading to uncertainty. Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: if 'today' is interpreted as expediting (ta'jil) and 'tomorrow' as a suspension (ta'liq), then the contract can be valid; otherwise, it is invalid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) allow both conditions regardless, while Zufar rejects both. The commentary delves into the reasoning: in the type case, the two works are clearly distinct contracts, so no issue. In the time case, associating a single work with two wages creates uncertainty unless one wage is interpreted figuratively. The discussion also addresses an objection from al-Kafi: why Imam treats 'today' differently in the tailor case (where he invalidated) versus here (where he validates by interpreting as expediting)? The answer is that in the tailor case, the delay was not accompanied by a decrease in wage as an incentive, so the literal timing was intended, making the contract invalid. Here, the decrease in wage for tomorrow serves as evidence for figurative interpretation. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of resolving uncertainty (jahalah) through interpretation and the importance of understanding the parties' intent.

Key Terms
ترديد الأجرة (taraddad al-ujrah): Making the wage variable between two or more specified amounts depending on a condition (e.g., type of work or time of performance).
أجير مشترك (ajir mushtarak): A hired worker who works for multiple people or on multiple tasks, not exclusively for one; here, if the work is specified, he becomes a common worker.
أجير خاص (ajir khas): A hired worker who is exclusive to one employer for a specific time; here, if time is specified, he becomes a private worker.
جهالة (jahalah): Uncertainty or ambiguity in the contract terms that can lead to dispute; the text discusses how it is resolved differently in sale vs. hire.
خيار التعين (khiyar al-ta'yin): Option of specification: a choice in a contract to select one of several options; in sale it requires explicit stipulation, but in hire it is not required for variable wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa's view in the passage, what is the ruling on the time-based variation (e.g., 'if you stitch today then for two dirhams, if tomorrow then for half a dirham')?
A) Valid unconditionally.
B) Invalid unconditionally.
C) Valid only if 'today' is interpreted as expediting and 'tomorrow' as suspension.
D) Valid only if the wage for tomorrow is higher.

Key Takeaway
Variable wage by type is always valid; variable wage by time is valid under Imam Abu Hanifa's relied-upon view if interpreted figuratively to avoid uncertainty.

Wage Variation for the Special Hireling: Ta'jil vs Ta'qit
Intra-Hanafi dispute on special hireling with wage variation by day or work type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a special hireling when the wage varies by day, and distinguish between the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
For a special hireling, time mention can be an incentive (ta'jil), not a condition, saving the contract from gharar.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq dives into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when a special hireling (ajīr khāṣṣ) is hired with a wage that depends on which day the work is done? Imam Abu Hanifa views the mention of 'today' as a nudge for speed rather than a fixed deadline, while the Sahibayn see it as a binding condition that introduces uncertainty. Understanding this clash reveals how Hanafi jurists balance contractual freedom with the prohibition of gharar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hireling type and the disputed scenario
Recognise that the case involves a special hireling (ajir khas), whose wage is due upon presenting himself for work, not necessarily upon completing it. The dispute centres on a contract that ties wage to the day of work (e.g., 'one dirham if today, half if tomorrow').
Special hirelings are distinguished from common hirelings (ajir mushtarak) whose wage is earned by actual work.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Imam holds the contract valid, treating the day mention as ta'jil (expedition) – an incentive for early completion. His proof includes the shepherd case (where time and work combine, yet ijarah is valid by consensus) and the analogy of work-type variation (Roman vs Persian sewing) which is allowed because wage becomes definite after work.
Imam's view relies on istihsan and the principle that uncertainty (gharar) can be resolved later if the wage is known per scenario.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that both wage and work are unknown due to two possible outcomes, making the contract invalid (fasid) due to gharar. For them, the wage is due upon delivery of self (taslim) before work, so uncertainty cannot be removed later.
The Sahibayn view the time mention as ta'qit (timing) – a strict condition that must be fulfilled for the named wage.
4
Analyse the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If work is done on the second day: Imam gives ajr al-mithl (equivalent wage) capped at the lower named wage; Sahibayn declare the contract invalid and the hireling may get nothing (or ajr al-mithl depending on sub-riwayat). The difference affects whether the contract stands or falls.
The matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) follows Imam's view, but later texts authenticate multiple narrations.
5
Consider the sub-cases and tarjih
The passage also covers scenarios where the wage is completely dropped for the second day, or where the contract is confined to one day, and notes the correction of Ibn Sama'a's narration. The mufta bihi is the position of Imam, but with nuances from later authorities.
Students should note the complexity: there are at least two riwayat within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عن
قال صاحب الكافي : وفي المسألة إشكال على قول الإمام حيث جعل ذكر اليوم للتعجيل ههنا حتى أجاز العقد، وفي مسألة الخياط جعله للتوقيت وأفسد العقد. والجواب أن ذكر اليوم حقيقة للتوقيت فيحمل عليه حتى يقوم الدليل على المجاز وهو نقصان الأجر بسبب التأخير الحقيقة ولم نعمم هناك وكان التوقيت مراداً ففسد العقد. وقوله «ترديد الأجرة» قيد اتفاقي لأنه لا فرق بين ترديد الأجرة ونفيها لما قال في المحيط البرهاني : لو قال إن خطته اليوم درهم وإن خطته غداً فلا أجر لك قال محمد في الإملاء : إن خاطه في اليوم الأول فله درهم، وإن خاطه في اليوم الثاني فله أجر مثله لا يزاد على درهم في قولهم جميعاً لأن إسقاط الأجر في اليوم الثاني لا ينفي وجوبه في اليوم الأول، ونفي التسمية في اليوم الأول لا ينفي أصل العقد فكان في اليوم الثاني عقد لا تسمية فيه فيجب أجر المثل ا هـ بلفظه . وفي التتارخانية بعد أن ذكر هذا الفرع، هذا إذا جمع بين الأمرين فلو أفرد العقد على اليوم بأن قال إن خطته اليوم فلك درهم ولم يزد على هذا فخاطه في الغد لم يذكر محمد هذا في شيء من الكتب، وكان الفقيه أبو بكر البلخي يقول على قولهما يستحق أجر المثل إذا خاطه في غد. وعلى قول الإمام لقائل أن يقول يجب، ولقائل أن يقول لا يجب ذلك وإن يقول هذا العقد هنا فاسد على قول الإمام لأنه جمع بين الوقت والعمل ولم تقم قرينة على أنه أراد بالوقت التعجيل فما وجه القول بالصحة؟ وفي العتابية : إن خطته اليوم فلك درهم وإن خطته في غد فلا شيء لك فسد العقد لأنه شرط القمار وقيل يصح في اليوم ويفسد في الغد، ولو قال ما خاطه اليوم فبحساب درهم وما خاطه غداً فبحساب نصف درهم يفسد لأنه الغد بلا خلاف فإن خاطه في الغد فله أجر مثله لا يزاد على درهم ولا ينقص من : نصف درهم، وهذا يشير إلى أنه يجوز أن يزيد على نصف درهم وهو رواية الأصل. وفي المسألة روايتان، وصحح رواية ابن سماعة وهو الصحيح اليوم. قال في الغياثية : ولو بدأ بالغد ثم اليوم فعند الإمام الصحيح هو الأول. وفي إجارة الأصل : لو قال إن خطته اليوم فلك درهم وإن لم تفرغ منه اليوم فلك نصف درهم ذكر الخلاف على نحو ما ذكر في المتن .
Book of Ijarah, Chapter on Guarantee of the Hireling. And in the second case, [he is] a special hireling. If he sews it tomorrow, he gets its equivalent wage, not exceeding half a dirham, unlike the Persian and Roman [cloth] because they are two different contracts that did not combine, so they differ. And it is problematic regarding what was reasoned with in the case of today and tomorrow: the case of the shepherd, for it combined mention of time and work, and the ijarah is valid by agreement. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discusses the ruling for a special hireling (ajir khas) when the wage is varied based on the day of work or the type of work. The author first distinguishes between a common hireling (ajir mushtarak) and a special hireling (ajir khas). The main scenario: if a tailor is hired to sew a garment and the wage is specified as one dirham if done today or half a dirham if tomorrow, there are differing opinions. Imam Abu Hanifa considers the mention of 'today' as a stipulation for expediting the work (ta'jil) rather than a strict time condition, so the contract is valid even if sewed the next day, but the wage is reduced to the equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) view it as a time condition making the contract invalid for the later day due to uncertainty (gharar). The text also discusses similar cases for Roman and Persian sewing, the shepherd case, and various sub-rulings. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Imam Abu Hanifa as per the matn, but there are internal Hanafi debates.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): A special hireling whose services are exclusively for the hirer for a specific period; wage is due upon delivery of self even without work.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The market-equivalent wage determined by the court when no named wage exists in the contract.
ترديد الأجرة (tardīd al-ujrah): Stipulating different wages for different days or types of work in the same contract.
التعجيل (al-ta'jīl): Interpretation of a time mention as an incentive to expedite work, not as a binding condition.
التوقيت (al-tawqīt): Interpretation of a time mention as a binding deadline or condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A special hireling is hired with the condition: 'If you sew it today, you get one dirham; if you sew it tomorrow, you get half a dirham.' According to the mufta bihi position, if he sews it tomorrow, what does he receive?
A) One dirham
B) Half a dirham
C) Equivalent wage (ajr al-mithl) not exceeding half a dirham
D) Nothing, because the contract is invalid

Key Takeaway
For a special hireling, a wage that varies by the day of work is valid if the time mention is interpreted as an incentive (ta'jil) rather than a strict condition, with ajr al-mithl due for delayed work.

Variable Wages in Ijara: Dispute Between Imam and Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on variable-rental wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute on variable-rental wages and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A variable wage known at contract is valid in potential; uncertainty resolved upon actual use.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute in rental contracts (ijara). The question: Is it permissible to make the rental wage depend on the type of work the hirer chooses? For example, renting a shop with two wages: one for use as a blacksmith, another for use as a perfumer. Imam Abu Hanifa says yes; his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, say no. We will explore their proofs and the practical effect of their disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
Understand the scenario: a rental contract where the wage is variable based on the benefit (e.g., blacksmith vs. perfumer shop; different distances or loads for an animal).
The wage is stated in the contract but not fixed until the hirer chooses the use.
2
State the positions
Imam Abu Hanifa holds the contract valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it invalid due to uncertainty in both wage and benefit.
The dispute is recorded in the zahir al-riwayah.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
They argue that for a specific hireling (ajir khas), the wage becomes due upon delivery (taslim), even without work. At the moment of delivery, it is unknown which wage applies, making both wage and benefit unknown.
This is unlike tailoring (Roman/Persian) where wage is earned only after work, which resolves uncertainty.
4
Analyze the Imam's proof
The Imam compares the case to tailoring: the hirer chooses one of two distinct benefits, each with a known wage. The contract is for benefit, and upon actual use the uncertainty disappears. The hirer voluntarily accepts the risk.
The Imam also distinguishes from variation in time (day/tomorrow), where wage is due after time passes, not after work.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to the Imam, the contract is valid and enforceable with the agreed variable wage. According to the Sahibayn, the contract is void (fasid) and only the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) is due if work was done. Also, later scholars differed on what wage is due if the object is delivered but not used.
The mufta bihi (operative view) is the Imam's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الدكان والبيت والدابة مسافة وحملا) يعني يجوز أن يجعل الأجر متردداً في الدكان بأن يقول إن سكنت حداداً فبدرهمين وإن سكنت عطار فبدرهم، أو يتردد بين مسافتين في الدابة أو بين حملين بأن يقول إن ذهب إلى بغداد بكذا وإلى الكوفة بكذا، أو إن حملت قطناً فبكذا وإن حملت حديداً فبكذا وهذا قول الإمام وعندهما لا تجوز هذه الإجارة. لهما أن الأجرة والمنفعة مجهولتان لأن الأجر في الأجير الخاص يجب بالتسليم من غير عمل ولا يدري أي العملين يقدر ولا أي التسميتين تجب وقت التسليم بخلاف خياطة الرومية والفارسية لأن الإجارة لا تجب فيه إلا بالعمل وبه ترفع الجهالة، وبخلاف الترديد في اليوم والغد لأنه عندهما كمسألة الرومية أو الفارسية فلا يجب الأجر إلا بعد العمل، فعند هذا ذلك هو معلوم . القاعدة هو . فإن قلت : فما الفرق على قولهما بين الترديد في العمل والزمان حيث جوزاها ومعناه في البيت والدكان والإمام جوز هنا ومنع في الزمان؟ قلت : قالا : التفاوت في السكنى فاحشة فمنعاه والإمام قال : هو رضي بإدخال الضرر على نفسه فأجازه وللإمام أنه خيره بين شيئين متغايرين وجعل لكل واحد منهما أجراً معلوماً فوجب أن يجوز كما في الرومية والفارسية والإجارة تعقد للانتفاع فالظاهر أن يستوفي المنافع وعند الاستيفاء ترفع الجهالة بخلاف الترديد في اليوم والغد على ما تقدم وهنا يجوز الترديد بين شيئين بأن يقول أجرتك هذه الدار كل شهر بمائة أو هذه الدار بمائتين أو هذه الدار بثلاثمائة، ولا يجوز بين أكثر من ذلك لما تقدم وفي الكبرى واختلف المشايخ على قول الإمام في مسألة الدابة والدار إذا سلم ولم يسكن ولم يحمل عليها ولم يركبها؛ قال بعضهم يجب أقل الأجرين وهو المقابل بأدنى العملين والزائد مشكوك فيه فلا يجب بالشك، وقال بعضهم إذا وجد التسليم ولم توجد المنفعة جعل التسليم لهما إذا ليس أحدهما بأولى من الآخر فيجب نصف آجر كل من الحداد والقصار ونصف أجر الحمل ونصف أجر الركوب. وفي التتارخانية : وذكر الكرخي من استأجر دابة من بغداد إلى البصرة بخمسة وإلى الكوفة بعشرة، فإن كانت المسافة إلى البصرة نصف المسافة إلى الكوفة فالعقد جائز، وإن كان أقل أو أكثر لا يجوز على قول محمد وقال الإمام يجوز. وفي نوادر هشام عن محمد: إذا قال لغيره إن حملت هذه الخشبة إلى موضع كذا فبدرهم، وإن حملت هذه الأخرى إلى موضع كذا فبدرهمين فحملهما إلى ذلك الموضع فله در همان وهو يخالف رواية ابن سماعة ا هـ
And regarding the shop, the house, and the animal for a distance and a load: meaning it is permissible to make the wage variable in the shop by saying: 'If you reside as a blacksmith, then for two dirhams; if you reside as a perfumer, then for one dirham.' Or to vary between two distances for the animal, or between two loads, by saying: 'If you go to Baghdad, for such-and-such; if you go to Kufa, for such-and-such.' Or: 'If you carry cotton, for such-and-such; if you carry iron, for such-and-such.' This is the statement of Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), this rental is not permissible. Their proof is that the wage and the benefit are unknown, because the wage for a specific hireling becomes due upon delivery without work, and it is not known which of the two tasks he will perform, nor which of the two named wages becomes due at the time of delivery. This is unlike the case of Roman and Persian tailoring, because the rental there is not due except with work, and with work the uncertainty is removed. And unlike the variation in day and tomorrow, because according to them it is like the case of Roman or Persian tailoring: the wage is not due except after work, so at that point it is known. The rule is... If you say: What is the difference according to their statement between variation in work and in time where they permit it? And its meaning is in the house and shop, and the Imam permitted here but prohibited in time? I say: They said: The disparity in residence is excessive, so they prohibited it. The Imam said: He consented to bringing harm upon himself, so he permitted it. And for the Imam, he gave him a choice between two different things and made for each a known wage, so it must be permitted, as in Roman and Persian tailoring. And the rental contract is made for benefit; the apparent case is that he will take the benefits, and at the time of taking, the uncertainty is removed, unlike the variation in day and tomorrow as previously. Here, variation between two things is permitted: saying 'I rent this house to you each month for a hundred, or this house for two hundred, or this house for three hundred.' But it is not permitted between more than that due to what preceded. And in al-Kubra: The mashayikh differed on the statement of the Imam regarding the case of the animal and the house: if he delivered and did not reside or load or ride? Some said: The lesser of the two wages is obligatory, which corresponds to the lesser task, and the extra is doubtful, so it is not obligatory due to doubt. Some said: Since delivery occurred but benefit did not, the delivery is assigned to both, since one is not more entitled than the other, so half the wage of the blacksmith and fuller, and half the wage of the load and riding, are obligatory. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: al-Karkhi mentioned: Whoever hires an animal from Baghdad to Basra for five and to Kufa for ten: if the distance to Basra is half the distance to Kufa, the contract is valid; if it is less or more, it is not valid according to Muhammad, and the Imam said it is valid. And in Nawadir Hisham from Muhammad: If he says to another, 'If you carry this piece of wood to such a place, for one dirham; if you carry this other piece to such a place, for two dirhams,' and he carries both to that place, he gets two dirhams. And this contradicts the narration of Ibn Sam'a, end.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of rental contracts (ijara) where the wage is made variable depending on the type of benefit (use of shop, distance traveled, load carried). Imam Abu Hanifa permits such contracts, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), consider them invalid due to uncertainty (jahala) in both the wage and the benefit. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the reasoning: According to the Sahibayn, the wage for a specific hireling (ajir khas) becomes due upon delivery (taslim) of the hired object, regardless of actual work. Since at the time of delivery it is unknown which task the hirer will choose, both the wage and the benefit are uncertain. This is unlike hiring for a specific type of tailoring (Roman or Persian), where the wage is only due after work, and the work clarifies the wage. Likewise, variation in time (e.g., day vs. tomorrow) is permissible because the wage is due after the time passes. The Imam argues that the hirer chooses one of two distinct benefits, each with a known wage. The benefit will be realized later, removing uncertainty. The Imam also invokes the principle that the hirer voluntarily accepts potential harm. The passage then discusses a secondary ikhtilaf among later scholars: if the rented house or animal is delivered but not used, what wage is due? Two opinions: either the minimum wage or half of each. Additional rulings from al-Tatarkhaniyya and Nawadir are cited, showing that if the distance is exactly half, the contract is valid according to Muhammad (a concession), but the Imam permits it absolutely. The lesson highlights the Hanafi method of qiyas and istihsan in resolving rental disputes.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): A specific hireling whose wage becomes due upon delivery of the hired object, even without work.
جهالة (jahāla): Uncertainty or ambiguity in the essential terms (wage or benefit) that renders a contract invalid.
رومية وفارسية (rūmiyya wa fārisiyya): Two types of tailoring: Roman (Byzantine) and Persian. Used as examples of specific tasks where the wage is known after work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in a variable-wage rental contract?
A) According to the Imam, the contract is valid and the agreed wage is due; according to the Sahibayn, it is void and the fair wage is due.
B) Both agree the contract is valid, but differ on the wage amount.
C) According to the Imam, the contract is void; according to the Sahibayn, it is valid.
D) Both agree the contract is void due to jahala.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a rental contract with variable wages based on the hirer's choice of benefit is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and the uncertainty is resolved upon actual use.

Restriction on Traveling with a Hired Slave for Service
Ruling on not traveling with a hired slave unless specified as a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on traveling with a hired slave and explain how custom ('urf) and the principle of harm function as the legal proofs (dalil).

Core Idea
Custom binds a hired slave's service to residence; travel requires explicit permission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains why a hirer of a slave for service cannot travel with him without a condition. The key is the Hanafi principle that custom ('urf) is like a stipulated condition (al-ma'ruf ka-al-mashrut). The absolute contract is understood to cover only residence-based service, which is the common and predominant use. Traveling is more arduous and imposes the burden of return on the owner, causing harm. The lesson unpacks this reasoning and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: traveling with a hired slave for service without a condition. The ruling: it is not permissible; the hirer does not have the right to compel travel.
The ruling is not that travel is haram, but that the hirer lacks the contractual right.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is not a single text but a combination of custom ('urf) and the principle of removing harm (darar). Custom shows that hiring for service normally means residence. Harm arises because the owner bears the cost of return.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) grounded in observable practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The absolute contract (mutaq al-'aqd) is restricted by custom to residence, which is the general and predominant use. Custom acts as an implicit condition. Travel is more arduous and imposes the cost of return on the owner, causing harm. The hirer cannot impose harm without explicit permission.
The principle 'al-ma'ruf ka-al-mashrut' is central.
4
Note the exception and its basis
A slave bequeathed for service (al-mawsi bi-khidmatihi) is not restricted to residence because the burden of return is on the legatee, not the owner, and custom does not apply to a bequest.
This contrast highlights that the ruling hinges on harm to the owner.
5
State the consequence of violation
If the hirer travels with the slave anyway, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and loses the wage, because liability (daman) and wage cannot combine.
Even if the slave returns safely, no wage is owed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يسافر بعبد استأجره للخدمة بلا شرط لأن مطلق العقد تناول الخدمة في الإقامة وهو الأعم الأغلب وعليه عرف الناس فانصرف إليه فلا يكون له أن ينقله إلى خدمة السفر لأنه أشق، ولأن مؤنة الرد على المولى فيلحقه ضرر بذلك فلا يملكه إلا بإذنه بخلاف العبد الموصي بخدمته حيث لا يتقيد بالحضر لأن مؤنة الرد عليه ولم يوجد العرف في حقه. لا يقال لما ملك المنفعة ملك أن يسافر به كالمولى لأنا نقول : المولى إنما ملك ذلك لأنه ملك الرقبة. قيد بقوله «ولا يسافر» فأفاد أن له أن يستعمل فيما دون السفر ففي المحيط : استأجر عبداً ليخدمه ولم يبين مكان الخدمة له أن يستخدمه بالكوفة دون خارج الكوفة. قال شمس الأئمة: يعني لا يسافر بالعبد وله أن يخرجه إلى القرى وأفنية المصر ويستخدمه إلى العشاء الأخيرة، وليس له أن يضربه، وله أن يكلفه أنواع الخدمة ويخدم ضيفانه .وامرأته وأطلق في قوله «ولا يسافر» وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن متهيئاً للسفر وقد عرف بذلك لأن المعروف کالمشروط. ولو سافر به صار غاصباً ولا أجر عليه إن سلم لأن الضمان والأجر لا يجتمعان. وفي المحيط : لا يكلفه الخبز والطبخ والخياطة وعلف الدواب قال : تفسيره أن يعقده خياطاً ليخيط للناس أو خبازاً ليخبز للناس لأنه ليس من الخدمة بل من التجارة، وأما إذا خاط له وخبز له فله ذلك لأنه من أنواع الخدمة ولو دفع عبده إلى خائك ليعلمه النسج واشترط عليه أن يحدقه في ثلاثة أشهر ولم يجز لأن التحديق ليس بعلم معلوم، ولو أجر عبده سنة فأعتق العبد في خلال السنة جاز عتقه والعبد بالخيار إن شار أجاز العقد فيما بقي وله أجر ما بقي من السنة، وإن شاء فسخ : وليس للعبد أن يقبض الأجرة إلا بوكالة من المولى فإن كان المولى قبض الأجرة معجلاً فأعتق العبد من خلال السنة ؛ فإن أجاز العبد العقد فيما بقي سلم ذلك للسيد، ولو كان العبد هو الذي أجر نفسه بإذن المولى ثم أعتق العبد فله الخيار كما تقدم إلا أن العبد هو الذي يقبض الأجرة. وفي الغياثية : وإن قبض المولى جميع الأجرة قبل عتقه فذلك له إن لم يكن على العبد دين وإن كان صرف إلى غرمائه والفضل له لأنه كسب عبده . وأفاد قوله «استأجر عبداً» أن كلاً منهما ذكر لأنه لو استأجر أمة لا بد فيه من تفصيل، أو استأجر المرأة ذكر التخدمه لا بد فيه من تفصيل أو استأجرت حراً لا بد فيه من تفصيل، ولو أجر عبده سنة فأقام العبد بينة أن مولاه أعتقه قبل الإجارة فالأجرة للعبد، ولو قال العبد أنا حر وقد فسخت الإجارة فلم يقم بينة ودفعه القاضي إلى مولاه فأجبر على العمل فأقام بينة أنه حر وإن المولى أعتقه قبل الإجارة فلا أجر للعبد لأنه لو لم يقل فسخت كان الأجر للعبد، ولو كان غير بالغ وادعى العتق وقد أخره وقال فسخت ثم عمل فالأجرة للغلام اهـ مختصراً. وفي التتارخانية : ويكره للرجال أن يستأجر امرأة للخدمة حرة كانت أو أمة وإن كان له عيال فلا بأس بذلك إذا كان ثقة وبه يفتي ولو استأجر الرجل امرأته للخدمة لا يجوز أجر لها ولو لغسل الثياب والخياطة يجوز. ولو استأجرت المرأة زوجها للخدمة لا يجوز ولا أجر عليها لو خدم ولو
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: And he should not travel with a slave he hired for service without a condition, because the absolute contract encompasses service in residence, which is more general and predominant, and upon this is the custom of people, so it is restricted to that. Thus he may not transfer him to the service of travel, because it is more arduous, and because the expense of return is upon the owner, so harm would befall him thereby. Therefore he does not have the right to do so except with his permission. Unlike the slave bequeathed with his service, who is not restricted to residence, because the expense of return is upon the legatee, and custom does not apply in his case. It should not be said: Since he owns the benefit, he owns the right to travel with him like the owner? For we say: The owner only owns that because he owns the raqaba (the slave himself). He restricted with his statement 'and he should not travel': this indicates that he may use him for less than travel. In al-Muhit: He hired a slave to serve him and did not specify the place of service; he may use him in Kufa but not outside Kufa. Shams al-A'imma said: It means he should not travel with the slave, but he may take him to villages and courtyards of the city, and use him until the last 'isha prayer, and he may not hit him, and he may require various types of service, and he serves his guests and his wife. And he made his statement 'and he should not travel' absolute, but it is restricted to when he is not prepared for travel, and it is known by that because what is known is like a condition. And if he travels with him, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and no wage is due upon safe arrival, because liability (daman) and wage do not combine. In al-Muhit: He may not require him to bake bread, cook, sew, and fodder the animals. He said: Its interpretation is that he hired him as a tailor to sew for people or as a baker to bake for people, because that is not service but trade. But if he sews for him or bakes for him, he may do so because it is a type of service. And if he gave his slave to a weaver to teach him weaving and stipulated that he should accomplish it in three months, it is not permissible because accomplishment is not known knowledge. And if he leased his slave for a year and the slave was freed during the year: his emancipation is valid, and the slave has the option: if he wishes, he may validate the contract for the remainder and have the wage for the remainder of the year; if he wishes, he may rescind. The slave may not receive the wage except with a proxy from the master. If the master received the wage in advance and then freed the slave during the year: if the slave validates the contract for the remainder, that wage goes to the master. And if the slave leased himself with the master's permission and then was freed, he has the option as before, except that the slave himself receives the wage. In al-Ghiyathiyya: If the master received all the wage before emancipation, it is his unless the slave had a debt; if there was a debt, it is paid to creditors, and the surplus is for him because it is his slave's earning. And his statement 'he hired a slave' indicates that it is mentioned for each? Because if he hired a female slave, detail is necessary; or if he hired a woman, detail is necessary; or if he hired a free man, detail is necessary. And if he leased his slave for a year, and the slave produced proof that his master freed him before the lease, the wage is for the slave. And if the slave said 'I am free and I have rescinded the lease' without proof, and the judge handed him to his master and he was forced to work, then he produced proof that he was free and the master freed him before the lease, then no wage is due to the slave, because if he had not said 'I rescinded', the wage would be for the slave. And if he was a minor and claimed emancipation and postponed it and said 'I rescinded' then worked, the wage is for the boy, end summary. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: It is disliked (makruh) for men to hire a woman for service, whether free or slave; but if he has dependents, there is no harm if he is trustworthy, and this is the fatwa. And if a man hires his wife for service, no wage is valid for her; but for washing clothes and sewing, it is permissible. And if a woman hires her husband for service, it is not valid and no wage is due on her if he serves, and if...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage begins with the ruling that a person who hires a slave for service (without specifying a condition) may not travel with the slave. The reason is that the absolute contract ('itlaq al-'aqd) is understood by custom ('urf) to mean service in the place of residence (hadar), which is the common and predominant use. Traveling is more arduous and additionally places the burden of returning the slave on the owner (mawla), causing harm. Therefore, the hirer cannot compel travel without explicit permission. This is contrasted with a slave bequeathed with his service (al-mawsi bi-khidmatihi), where the legatee can take him on travel because the burden of return is on the legatee, and the custom of limiting to residence does not apply. The author then addresses a potential objection: Why cannot the hirer travel as the owner can? The answer: The owner owns the raqaba (the slave itself), not just the benefit. From this main ruling, many sub-rulings branch out: the hirer may take the slave to villages and city outskirts, work him until late, but may not beat him. If he does travel, he becomes a usurper (ghasib) and the wage is canceled because liability and wage cannot coexist. Regarding the type of work, the hirer cannot force the slave into trade (like tailoring for public), but can have him do personal sewing or baking as part of service. Then the passage discusses the scenario of manumission during the lease term: if a leased slave is freed, he has the option to continue or rescind the lease. The master's advance payment is handled depending on debts. If a slave claims freedom and rescinds, but later proves it, the wage issue depends on his initial statement. The lesson ends with rulings on hiring women and spouses: it is generally disliked for a man to hire a woman for service unless he has dependents and is trustworthy; hiring one's spouse for service is invalid except for laundry and sewing. The passage covers a wide range of practical issues related to hiring slaves for service.

Key Terms
أجير خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): A specific hireling (here a slave) whose wage is due upon delivery (taslim) and whose benefit is limited by custom.
المعروف كالمشروط (al-maʿrūf ka-al-mashrūṭ): What is customary is like a stipulated condition: custom ('urf) governs the default scope of the contract.
غاصب (ghāṣib): A usurper: one who takes or uses property without right. Here, if he travels with the slave without permission, he becomes a usurper and loses the wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the consequence if a hirer travels with a hired slave without permission and the slave returns safely?
A) The hirer must pay the wage but is considered a usurper.
B) The hirer owes no wage and becomes a usurper.
C) The hirer must pay double the wage as compensation.
D) The slave is automatically freed.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) restricts a hired slave's service to residence; travel requires explicit condition, and violation makes the hirer a usurper with no wage due.

Ruling on Traveling with a Hired Slave for Service
Explaining when a hirer may travel with a hired slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of custom ('urf) to determine the scope of an ijarah contract and identify when a hirer may or may not travel with a hired slave.

Core Idea
Custom defines the default scope of an ijarah contract; travel is not included without permission.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key limitation on a hirer's rights when hiring a slave for service. You might think that owning the usufruct gives full freedom, but Hanafi law restricts it based on custom and potential harm to the owner. Let's see how custom ('urf) operates as a source of law in ijarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Default Ruling
The act is hiring a slave for service without specifying location. The default understanding is that the service is for residence (the city or town), not for travel.
This is based on the common custom ('urf) of the people.
2
Locate the Primary Evidence
The custom ('urf) is the evidence. The text states that the absolute contract is diverted to the most common and prevalent practice (al-a'am wa al-aghall), which is residence.
Custom is considered like a stipulated condition (al-ma'ruf ka al-mashrut).
3
Understand the Distinction from the Owner's Travel
A potential qiyas: the hirer owns the usufruct, so why can't he travel like the owner? The rebuttal: the owner owns the slave itself (raqaba), not just the usufruct.
The owner's right to travel is based on ownership of the corpus.
4
Note the Practical Qualifications
The hirer may take the slave to villages within the outskirts of the city, use him until the last isha prayer, and assign various services. He may not beat the slave.
The prohibition on travel is restricted to when the slave is not prepared for travel.
5
Consequences of Violation
If the hirer travels with the slave, he becomes a usurper (ghāṣib) and is not liable for the wage if the slave is safe, because guarantee and wage do not combine.
This ruling is based on the Hanafi position that the custom is like a stipulated condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يسافر بعبد استأجره للخدمة بلا شرط لأن مطلق العقد تناول الخدمة في الإقامة وهو الأعم الأغلب وعليه عرف الناس فانصرف إليه فلا يكون له أن ينقله إلى خدمة السفر لأنه أشق، ولأن مؤنة الرد على المولى فيلحقه ضرر بذلك فلا يملكه إلا بإذنه بخلاف العبد الموصي بخدمته حيث لا يتقيد بالحضر لأن مؤنة الرد عليه ولم يوجد العرف في حقه. لا يقال لما ملك المنفعة ملك أن يسافر به كالمولى لأنا نقول : المولى إنما ملك ذلك لأنه ملك الرقبة. قيد بقوله «ولا يسافر» فأفاد أن له أن يستعمل فيما دون السفر ففي المحيط : استأجر عبداً ليخدمه ولم يبين مكان الخدمة له أن يستخدمه بالكوفة دون خارج الكوفة. قال شمس الأئمة: يعني لا يسافر بالعبد وله أن يخرجه إلى القرى وأفنية المصر ويستخدمه إلى العشاء الأخيرة، وليس له أن يضربه، وله أن يكلفه أنواع الخدمة ويخدم ضيفانه .وامرأته وأطلق في قوله «ولا يسافر» وهو مقيد بما إذا لم يكن متهيئاً للسفر وقد عرف بذلك لأن المعروف کالمشروط. ولو سافر به صار غاصباً ولا أجر عليه إن سلم لأن الضمان والأجر لا يجتمعان.
He travels with a slave he hired for service without condition because the absolute contract takes the service in residence, and it is the most common and prevalent, and people's custom is upon it, so it is diverted to it. Therefore, he cannot transfer him to travel service because it is more burdensome, and because the expense of return is upon the owner, so harm befalls him by that, so he does not own it except with his permission, unlike the slave who is bequeathed his service where he is not restricted to residence because the expense of return is upon him and custom is not found in his case. It cannot be said: since he owns the usufruct, he owns traveling with him like the owner, because we say: the owner owns that because he owns the corpus. He restricted by his saying: "and he does not travel," so it indicates that he may use him in less than travel. In al-Muhit: He hired a slave to serve him and did not specify the place of service; he may use him in Kufa but not outside Kufa. Shams al-A'imma said: meaning he does not travel with the slave, but he may take him out to villages and outskirts of the city and use him until the last isha prayer, and he may not beat him, and he may assign him types of service and serve his guests and his wife. And he made absolute in his saying "and he does not travel," and it is restricted to when he is not prepared for travel, and it is known by that because the known is like the stipulated. And if he travels with him, he becomes a usurper and no wage is due upon him if he is safe, because guarantee and wage do not combine.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the hire of a slave for service. The author explains that when a person hires a slave for service without specifying travel, the contract is understood by default to cover service only in the place of residence (the city or town) because custom ('urf) dictates that hiring for service is predominantly for residence. The hirer therefore does not have the right to take the slave on a journey unless he obtains the owner's permission, since travel is more burdensome and the owner would bear the cost of return. The author refutes a potential qiyas: one might argue that since the hirer owns the usufruct, he should be able to travel like the owner; but the distinction is that the owner owns the slave itself (raqaba), not just the usufruct. The text then qualifies the ruling: the phrase 'nor does he travel' means he cannot take him on a journey, but he may take him to villages within the outskirts of the city and use him until the last isha prayer. He may not beat the slave, but he may assign various services and serve his guests and wife. This ruling is conditioned on the slave not being already prepared for travel. If the hirer violates this and travels with the slave, he becomes a usurper (ghāṣib) and is not liable for the wage if the slave is safe, because guarantee of compensation and wage cannot coexist.

Key Terms
عبد (abd): a male slave owned by another
إجارة (ijarah): a contract of hire or lease
عرف (urf): custom as a source of law

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default understanding of a contract to hire a slave for service without specifying location?
A) The service is assumed to cover all locations including travel.
B) The service is assumed to cover only the place of residence due to custom.
C) The contract is void unless the location is specified.
D) The hirer may choose any location as long as it is reasonable.

Key Takeaway
Custom ('urf) operates as a binding condition in ijarah contracts, restricting the hirer from traveling with a hired slave without owner permission.

Permissible and Impermissible Tasks for a Hired Slave
Clarifying which tasks a hirer may and may not impose on a hired slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible personal service (khidmah) and impermissible trade (tijarah) tasks for a hired slave, and apply this distinction to determine the validity of a hiring contract.

Core Idea
Trade tasks for the public are not service; only personal tasks for the hirer are permissible.

When you hire a slave for service, what work can you require? The passage from al-Muhit clarifies that the hirer cannot turn the slave into a tradesman working for the public, because that falls under tijarah (trade), not khidmah (personal service). However, doing those same tasks for the hirer's own household is allowed. This distinction is crucial for the validity of the ijarah contract. Additionally, a teaching contract with an uncertain outcome is invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited tasks
The text lists baking, cooking, tailoring, feeding animals. These are trades when done for the public.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
Because these are trade (tijarah), not service (khidmah); trade is outside the scope of a service hire.
3
Distinguish the exception
If the same tasks are done for the hirer himself, they become permissible service.
4
Apply the rule to a teaching contract
Stipulating to perfect the slave in a fixed term is invalid because perfection is uncertain (jahalah).
5
Synthesize the principle
The hirer can only require tasks that directly serve him, not commercial activities for others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لا يكلفه الخبز والطبخ والخياطة وعلف الدواب قال : تفسيره أن يعقده خياطاً ليخيط للناس أو خبازاً ليخبز للناس لأنه ليس من الخدمة بل من التجارة، وأما إذا خاط له وخبز له فله ذلك لأنه من أنواع الخدمة ولو دفع عبده إلى خائك ليعلمه النسج واشترط عليه أن يحدقه في ثلاثة أشهر ولم يجز لأن التحديق ليس بعلم معلوم
And in al-Muhit: He does not require him (to do) baking, cooking, tailoring, and feeding animals. He said: its interpretation is that he contracts him as a tailor to sew for people or a baker to bake for people because that is not service but trade. But if he sews and bakes for him (the hirer), he has that because it is from the types of service. And if he gives his slave to a weaver to teach him weaving and stipulates that he refine him in three months, it is not permissible because refining is not a known knowledge.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Muhit within the commentary. It specifies that the hirer cannot force the hired slave to engage in trades like baking, cooking, tailoring, or feeding animals for the public, because those are trades (tijarah) not personal service (khidmah). However, if the slave performs these tasks for the hirer himself (such as baking or sewing for his own household), it is permissible because it falls under personal service. Additionally, if a person gives his slave to a weaver to teach him weaving and stipulates that the weaver must perfect him in three months, that contract is invalid because perfecting is not a fixed, known skill; the contract lacks certainty (jahalah).

Key Terms
خدمة (khidmah): personal service
تجارة (tijarah): trade or commerce for profit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a hirer force a hired slave to bake bread for the public?
A) Yes, because baking is a service.
B) No, because that is trade, not personal service.
C) Yes, with the owner's permission.
D) No, unless the slave agrees.

Key Takeaway
The hirer can only require personal service (khidmah) for himself, not trade (tijarah) for the public; uncertain stipulations are invalid.

Effect of Freeing a Hired Slave During the Lease Period
Rulings on the options when a hired slave is freed mid-term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options available to a slave freed during a lease and explain the wage distribution in the various scenarios presented in the text.

Core Idea
A freed slave can choose to continue or end the lease, and wages are apportioned accordingly.

When a hired slave is freed mid-term, several legal questions arise: does the lease continue? Who gets the wages? The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings, granting the freed slave an option to ratify or rescind, with careful rules about wage collection and the impact of advance payment. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains these scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Scenario and Ruling
Determine the basic case: master leases his slave for a year, then frees him during the year. Note that the freeing is valid and the slave has an option (khiyar).
The slave's freedom does not automatically void the lease.
2
Analyze the Slave's Options
Examine the two choices: ratify the contract for the remaining period (the slave gets wage for that period) or rescind. Consider who collects the wage: only by agency from the master.
If the master already took the wage in advance and the slave ratifies, the master keeps it.
3
Distinguish Cases by Who Hired the Slave
Compare when the master hired out the slave versus when the slave hired himself out with the master's permission. In the latter, the slave collects the wage directly.
The option remains the same but collection differs.
4
Examine the Sub-ruling from al-Ghiyathiyya
Consider the case where the master collected all wages before freeing: he keeps them unless the slave has debts, in which case wages go to creditors.
This is an exception based on the slave's debts.
5
Review Evidentiary Sub-rulings
Look at scenarios involving proof of prior freeing and the case of a minor slave. Understand how evidence and statement affect the wage entitlement.
If the slave rescinds before providing evidence, the ruling differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أجر عبده سنة فأعتق العبد في خلال السنة جاز عتقه والعبد بالخيار إن شار أجاز العقد فيما بقي وله أجر ما بقي من السنة، وإن شاء فسخ : وليس للعبد أن يقبض الأجرة إلا بوكالة من المولى فإن كان المولى قبض الأجرة معجلاً فأعتق العبد من خلال السنة ؛ فإن أجاز العبد العقد فيما بقي سلم ذلك للسيد، ولو كان العبد هو الذي أجر نفسه بإذن المولى ثم أعتق العبد فله الخيار كما تقدم إلا أن العبد هو الذي يقبض الأجرة. وفي الغياثية : وإن قبض المولى جميع الأجرة قبل عتقه فذلك له إن لم يكن على العبد دين وإن كان صرف إلى غرمائه والفضل له لأنه كسب عبده . وأفاد قوله «استأجر عبداً» أن كلاً منهما ذكر لأنه لو استأجر أمة لا بد فيه من تفصيل، أو استأجر المرأة ذكر التخدمه لا بد فيه من تفصيل أو استأجرت حراً لا بد فيه من تفصيل، ولو أجر عبده سنة فأقام العبد بينة أن مولاه أعتقه قبل الإجارة فالأجرة للعبد، ولو قال العبد أنا حر وقد فسخت الإجارة فلم يقم بينة ودفعه القاضي إلى مولاه فأجبر على العمل فأقام بينة أنه حر وإن المولى أعتقه قبل الإجارة فلا أجر للعبد لأنه لو لم يقل فسخت كان الأجر للعبد، ولو كان غير بالغ وادعى العتق وقد أخره وقال فسخت ثم عمل فالأجرة للغلام اهـ مختصراً.
And if he leases his slave for a year and then frees the slave during the year, his freeing is valid and the slave has the option: if he wishes, he may ratify the contract for the remaining period and he gets the wage for the remaining part of the year, and if he wishes, he may rescind. And the slave may not take the wage except by agency from the master. If the master took the wage in advance and then freed the slave during the year, then if the slave ratifies the contract for the remaining period, that wage is secured for the master. And if the slave himself hired himself out with the master's permission and then the slave was freed, he has the option as previously, except that the slave takes the wage. And in al-Ghiyathiyya: If the master took all the wage before his freeing, that is for him if there is no debt on the slave, and if there is debt, it is spent on his creditors and the surplus is for him because it is the earning of his slave. And his saying 'he hired a slave' indicates that each of them (male and female) is mentioned, because if he hired a female slave, there must be detail, or if a woman hires a male to serve her, there must be detail, or if she hires a free man, there must be detail. And if he leases his slave for a year and the slave presents evidence that his master freed him before the lease, then the wage is for the slave. And if the slave says 'I am free and I have rescinded the lease' and he did not establish evidence, and the judge handed him over to his master and he was forced to work, then he presents evidence that he is free and that the master freed him before the lease, then no wage is due to the slave because if he had not said 'I rescinded', the wage would have been for the slave. And if he was a minor and claimed freedom and delayed and said 'I rescind' and then worked, the wage is for the boy. End summary.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings regarding what happens when a hired slave is freed during the lease term. The main ruling: if the master leases his slave for a year and then frees him mid-term, the freeing is valid and the slave has the option to either continue the lease for the remainder (in which case he gets the wage for the remaining period) or to rescind the contract. However, the slave cannot collect the wage unless he is the agent of the master. If the master collected the full wage in advance and then freed the slave, and the slave ratifies the contract, the wage remains with the master. If the slave had leased himself out with the master's permission and then became free, he has the same option but can collect the wage himself. According to al-Ghiyathiyya, if the master collected all wages before freeing, he keeps them unless the slave has debts, in which case the wages go to creditors. The text also clarifies that the general wording 'he hired a slave' includes both male and female, but specific rulings apply. Additional sub-rulings deal with evidence of prior freeing and the case of a minor slave claiming freedom.

Key Terms
عتق (itq): emancipation of a slave
خيار (khiyar): option to annul or ratify a contract
إجارة (ijara): lease or hire contract
فسخ (faskh): rescission or annulment of a contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a slave is freed during the lease term, what option does he have regarding the remaining period?
A) He must continue working.
B) He may continue or rescind.
C) The lease is automatically void.
D) Only the master can decide.

Key Takeaway
A freed slave has the option to ratify or rescind the lease, with wages apportioned accordingly.

Rulings on Hiring Women, Relatives, and Non-Muslims for Service
Rules on hiring women, spouses, relatives, and Muslims to non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on hiring women, spouses, relatives, and non-Muslims for service and identify the exceptions based on specific conditions.

Core Idea
Hiring a wife for service is invalid, but a father can be hired for specific tasks; a Muslim may not serve a non-Muslim.

This passage from al-Tatar Khaniyya and Fatawa al-Fadli presents several rulings concerning who may be hired for service. The Hanafi school considers the nature of the work, the relationship between the parties, and the potential for fitna or disrespect. While some hires are outright invalid, others are disliked but permitted under certain conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person being hired and the type of work
Classify the hirer and the hiree (e.g., woman, wife, father, Muslim/non-Muslim) and the specific task (general service vs. specific work like washing or shepherding).
The ruling often depends on these two factors.
2
Determine the default ruling based on the relationship
For each relationship, note the default hukm: e.g., hiring a woman is makruh, hiring a spouse is invalid, hiring a father for service is invalid, hiring oneself to a non-Muslim for service is not permissible.
The default assumes general service.
3
Look for exceptions based on the nature of the work
Check if the passage specifies a different ruling for a particular task. For example, hiring a wife for washing clothes or sewing is permissible; hiring a father for grazing sheep is permissible.
Exceptions often involve non‑servile, respectful tasks.
4
Consider the status of the hirer for hiring women
If the hirer has dependents and is trustworthy, hiring a woman for service becomes permissible (the karaha is lifted).
This is a conditional exception.
5
Note the additional rule regarding hiring out to non-Muslims
A Muslim may not hire himself to a non-Muslim for service, but for other work (e.g., craftsmanship) it is permissible as per Fatawa al-Fadli.
This rule protects the Muslim’s dignity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التتارخانية : ويكره للرجال أن يستأجر امرأة للخدمة حرة كانت أو أمة وإن كان له عيال فلا بأس بذلك إذا كان ثقة وبه يفتي ولو استأجر الرجل امرأته للخدمة لا يجوز أجر لها ولو لغسل الثياب والخياطة يجوز. ولو استأجرت المرأة زوجها للخدمة لا يجوز ولا أجر عليها لو خدم ولو عبد محجور عليه أجراً دفعه لعمله ولا يضمن غاصب العبد ما أكل من أجره ولو استأجر أباه للخدمة لا يجوز ولا أجر له لا فرق بين الكافر والمسلم. ولو استأجر أباه لرعي غنمه يجوز، ولو استأجر أمه أو جدته للخدمة لا يجوز، ولو خدم فله المسمى. ولو استأجر عمه وهو أكبر منه أو أخاه وهو أكبر منه لا يجوز. وفي فتاوى الفضلي : لا يجوز إجارة المسلم نفسه من كافر في الخدمة وفيما غير الخدمة يجوز.
And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: It is disliked for men to hire a woman for service, whether free or slave, and if he has dependents, there is no harm in that if he is trustworthy, and according to this fatwa is given. And if a man hires his wife for service, no wage is permissible for her, but for washing clothes and sewing it is permissible. And if a woman hires her husband for service, it is not permissible and no wage is due upon her if he serves. And if a slave under interdiction (hires out) and pays the wage for his work, and the usurper of the slave does not guarantee what he ate from his wage, and if he hires his father for service, it is not permissible and no wage is due for him, no difference between disbeliever and Muslim. And if he hires his father to graze his sheep, it is permissible. And if he hires his mother or grandmother for service, it is not permissible, and if he serves, he gets the named wage. And if he hires his paternal uncle who is older than him or his brother who is older than him, it is not permissible. And in Fatawa al-Fadli: It is not permissible for a Muslim to hire himself to a disbeliever for service, but for other than service it is permissible.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage compiles several rulings from al-Tatar Khaniyya and Fatawa al-Fadli regarding who can be hired for service. Key points: (1) Men are discouraged (makruh) from hiring women for service, but if the man has dependents and is trustworthy, it is allowed; (2) Hiring one's wife for general service is invalid, but specific tasks like washing clothes and sewing are permissible; (3) A wife hiring her husband for service is invalid; (4) Hiring a father for service is invalid, but for a specific task like grazing sheep, it is valid; hiring a mother or grandmother is invalid; hiring an older uncle or older brother is invalid; (5) A Muslim may not hire himself out to a non-Muslim for service (khidmah), but for non-service work it is permissible. The rulings are based on the principle of maintaining respect for relatives and avoiding situations that undermine family dignity or lead to fitna.

Key Terms
كراهة (karaha): disliked (makruh)
محجور عليه (mahjur alayhi): a person under legal interdiction due to minority or insolvency
إجارة (ijara): hire, lease, employment contract
خدمة (khidma): service, often personal or domestic service

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always.
B) No, it is not permissible.
C) Yes, if the wage is high.
D) Only for household work.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of hiring in Hanafi fiqh hinges on the nature of the relationship, the type of work, and potential for loss of respect or fitna.
