والقول لرب الثوب في القميص والقباء والحمرة والصفرة والأجر وعدمه) يعني إذا اختلف رب الثوب والخياط في المخيط بأن قال رب الثوب أمرتك أن تعمل قباء وقال الخياط قميصاً، أو في لون الصبغ بأن قال رب الثوب أحمر وقال الصباغ أصفر، أو في الأجرة بأن قال صاحب الثوب عملته بغير أجرة وقال الصباغ بأجرة كان القول قول رب الثوب، وظاهر العبارة أنه لا فرق بين كون رب الثوب معروفاً بلبس ما نفاه أو لا، والذي يقتضيه النظر إن كان معروفاً بلبس ما نفاه أن يكون القول قول الخياط وإن لم يكن معروفاً أو جهل الحال يكون القول قول رب الثوب، أما إذا اختلفا في الخياطة والصبغ فلأن الإذن يستفاد منه فهو أعلم بكيفيته لأنه إذا أنكر الإذن أصلاً كان القول قوله فكذا إذا أنكر وصفه لأن الوصف تابع للأصل لكنه يحلف لأنه ادعى عليه شيئاً لو أقر به لزمه فإذا أنكره يحلف، فإذا حلف فالخياط ضامن وصاحب الثوب ضمير إن شاء ضمنه ثوباً غير معمول ولا أجر له أو قيمته معمولاً وله أجر مثله لا يجاوز به المسمى على ما بينا. وعن محمد: إنه يضمن ما زاد الصبغ فيه، لا يقال هذه مكررة مع قوله «ولو اختلفا في الإجارة قبل الاستيفاء إلى آخره لأنا نقول : هناك اتفقا على نوع العمل واختلفا في الأجرة وهنا اتفقا على الأجرة واختلفا في نوع العمل فلا تكرار، وأما إذا في الأجرة فلأن المستأجر ينكر تقوم عمله ووجوب الأجر والصباغ يدعيه فكان القول للمنكر وهذا قول الإمام. وقال الثاني : إن كان الصابغ حريفاً له أي معاملاً له بأن كان يدفع إليه شيئاً للعمل ويقاطعه عليه فله الأجر وإلا فلا. وقال محمد: إن كان الصابغ معروفاً بهذه الصنعة بالأجرة كان القول قوله وإلا فلا، لأنه لما فتح الدكان لذلك . ذلك جری مجرى التنصيص عليه اعتباراً بظاهر المقاصد . وقولهما استحسان والقياس قول الإمام والفتوى على قول محمد، فإن قلت : هذه متكررة مع قوله وبخياطة قباء وأمر بقميص فالجواب أن تلك باعتبار الضمان هو وهذا باعتبار أن القول لرب الثوب عند الاختلاف فلا تكرار وفي التتارخانية : ولو اختلف . والقصار في أجر الثوب فقال القصار بربع درهم وقال رب الثوب عملته بقيراط، فإن اختلفا قبل الشروع في العمل تحالفا وترادا، وإن كان بعد الفراغ من العمل فالقول قول رب الثوب ولم يحكم مقدار ما زادت القصارة فيه .اهـ والله أعلم .
The saying is the word of the owner of the garment regarding the shirt and the cloak, the red and the yellow, and the wage and its absence.) Means: If the owner of the garment and the tailor differ regarding the sewn garment: the owner says 'I ordered you to make a cloak' and the tailor says 'a shirt', or regarding the color of dye: the owner says 'red' and the dyer says 'yellow', or regarding the wage: the owner says 'you did it without wage' and the dyer says 'with wage', then the word is the word of the owner of the garment. The apparent wording indicates no distinction between the owner being known to wear that which he denies or not. But what reason requires is: if he is known to wear that which he denies, then the word is the word of the tailor; if he is not known or the situation is unknown, then the word is the word of the owner of the garment. As for when they differ regarding the tailoring and dyeing, it is because permission is derived from him, so he is most knowledgeable about its modality. Because if he denied the permission entirely, his word would be accepted; similarly if he denied its description, because the description follows the original. But he takes an oath because the other claims something against him which if acknowledged would be binding, so if he denies it, he takes an oath. If he swears, then the tailor is a guarantor, and the owner of the garment has the option: if he wishes, he may exact a garment not worked on and no wage for the tailor, or its value as worked and the tailor gets its wage not exceeding the named amount as we have explained. And from Muhammad: he guarantees the increase that the dye added. Let it not be said that this is repetitious with his saying 'If they differ regarding the lease before utilization' etc., because we say: there they agreed on the type of work and differed on the wage, while here they agreed on the wage and differed on the type of work, so there is no repetition. As for when they differ regarding the wage, it is because the hirer denies the value of his work and the obligation of wage, while the dyer claims it, so the word is the word of the denier. This is the statement of Imam. The second (Abu Yusuf) said: if the dyer is a habitual worker for him, i.e., a regular customer, such that he would give him something for work and settle accounts with him, then he gets the wage, otherwise not. Muhammad said: if the dyer is known for this craft for a wage, then his word is accepted, otherwise not, because when he opened the shop for that, it is akin to explicit stipulation, considering apparent intentions. Their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) statement is istihsan, the analogy is the statement of Imam, and the fatwa is on the statement of Muhammad. If you say: this is repetitious with his statement 'regarding tailoring a cloak and ordering a shirt', the answer is that that concerns guarantee, while this concerns that the word is the owner's at the time of dispute, so there is no repetition. In al-TatarKhaniyya: 'If the fuller and the owner differ regarding the wage of the cloth: the fuller says a quarter dirham and the owner says I worked it for a qirat; if they differ before commencing work, they both take oaths and rescind; if after completion of work, the word is the word of the owner, and the amount the fulling added is not adjudicated.' End. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on disputes between the owner of cloth and a craftsman (tailor or dyer). The general rule is that the owner's statement is given credence regarding the type of garment, color, and wage, because he is the one who gave permission. However, there is an exception based on custom: if the owner is known to wear what he denies, then the craftsman's statement is taken. The text then discusses the taking of oaths and the guarantee of the craftsman. It presents three intra-Hanafi opinions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the owner's word is always taken; Abu Yusuf adds a condition that if the dyer is a regular worker (harif), his word is accepted; and Muhammad al-Shaybani says the dyer's word is accepted if he is known in that trade with a wage. The relied-upon fatwa is on Muhammad's view due to custom and practice. The passage also distinguishes this dispute from a previous one about lease, and includes an additional ruling from al-TatarKhaniyya about the fuller.

Key Terms
القول لرب الثوب (al-qawl li-rabb al-thawb): The owner of the garment's statement is given credence in disputes with the craftsman
حريف (harīf): A regular customer or habitual worker; someone who repeatedly deals with the craftsman
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas for a preferable ruling based on custom or need

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a dispute between a cloth owner and a tailor about whether the garment was to be a shirt or a cloak, whose statement is accepted according to the relied-upon fatwa?
A) The tailor's statement
B) The owner's statement
C) The tailor's statement if he is known for the trade
D) The owner's statement only if he swears

Key Takeaway
When an owner and craftsman differ, the mufta bihi Hanafi position is to accept the craftsman's word if he is known in his trade, otherwise the owner's.
